Replacement of Lost or Worn-Out Clothing After Judicial Estimation
Ruling on whether the husband must replace clothing that is lost, stolen, or worn out before the period ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for when a husband must replace clothing or maintenance that is lost, stolen, or worn out before the judge's estimated period ends.

Core Idea
The judge's estimation stands unless actual use proves it wrong; misuse does not trigger replacement.

After a judge fixes clothing or maintenance for a wife, various events may occur: loss, theft, wear, or leftover after the period. The Hanafi school provides detailed criteria to determine whether the husband must provide anew. This lesson unpacks the principles of error in estimation (khata' fi al-taqdir) and how they apply to clothing and maintenance for wives versus relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenarios
The passage covers four situations: (1) clothing lost before the period, (2) clothing torn by misuse versus normal use, (3) clothing leftover after the period, and (4) analogous rules for maintenance money.
Each scenario has a distinct ruling based on whether the judge's estimation is proven erroneous.
2
Extract the ruling for loss or theft before the period
If the clothing is lost, stolen, or destroyed before the period ends, the husband does not have to replace it until the period passes. The judge's estimation is not revisited unless error becomes apparent.
This ruling is the baseline; exceptions depend on the cause of destruction.
3
Distinguish between misuse and normal wear
If the clothing is torn by misuse (e.g., deliberately damaged), the judge's estimation remains valid, so no replacement. If torn by normal use, the estimation was too low, so the husband must provide new clothing immediately.
The key is whether the wear indicates an error in the judge's assessment of the clothing's durability.
4
Apply the rule for leftover clothing after the period
If the period ends and the clothing remains intact, the judge's estimation is proven too generous; no new clothing is given unless the wife used another set simultaneously, showing the original was insufficient.
This contrasts with maintenance money, where leftover may be due to frugality, not error.
5
Contrast the wife's case with relatives
For relatives, any leftover after the period means no further provision because it is need-based. For the wife, it is compensation for confinement, so loss before the period triggers replacement even without error.
The different legal bases (mu'awada versus ihtiyaj) change the outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة: إذا فرض لها القاضي الكسوة فهلكت أو سرقت منها أو خرقتها قبل الوقت فليس عليه أن يكسوها حتى يمضي الوقت الذي لا تبقى إليه الكسوة. والأصل أن القاضي متى ظهر له الخطأ في التقدير يرده فإذا لم يظهر له ذلك لا يرده، فإن تخرقت الكسوة بالاستعمال قبل مضي الوقت ينظر ؛ فإن تخرقت بخرق استعمالها لم يتبين الخطأ في التقدير فلا يقضي بكسوة أخرى ما لم يمض ذلك الوقت، وإن تخرقت بالاستعمال المعتاد تبين الخطأ في التقدير فيقضي بكسوة أخرى، وكذا الجواب في النفقة إذا ضاعت أو سرقت أو أكلت أو أسرفت أو لم تسرف وكان ذلك قبل مضي الوقت فهو كما قلنا في الكسوة، ولو مضت المدة والكسوة باقية فإن لم تستعمل تلك الكسوة أصلاً حتى مضى الوقت يفرض القاضي لها كسوة أخرى لأنه لم يظهر خطأ القاضي في التقدير، وإن استعملت تلك الكسوة، فإن استعملت معها كسوة أخرى في تلك المدة يفرض لها القاضي كسوة أخرى في تلك المدة، وإن لم تستعمل مع هذه الكسوة كسوة أخرى لا يفرض لها أخرى لأنه ظهر خطؤه في التقدير حيث وقت وقتاً تبقى الكسوة وراء ذلك الوقت. فرق بين وبين ما إذا فرض لها القاضي عشرة دراهم نفقة شهر فمضى الشهر وقد بقي من العشرة شيء حيث يفرض لها القاضي في النفقة عشرة أخرى، والفرق أن في باب النفقة لم يظهر خطأ القاضي في التقدير بيقين الجواز أنه إنما بقي من العشرة شيء لتقتير وجد منها في الإنفاق على نفسها فبقي التقدير معتبراً فيقضي القاضي لها بعشرة أخرى، أما في باب الكسوة إذا لبست جميع المدة ولم تتخرق فقد ظهر خطأ القاضي في التقدير بيقين لأنا تيقنا أنه لم يوجد منها التقتير في اللبس. فرق بين نفقة الزوجات وكسوتهن وبين نفقة المحارم وكسوتهم فإن في الأقارب إذا مضى الوقت وبقي شيء من الدراهم أو الكسوة فإن القاضي لا يقضي بأخرى في الأحوال كلها لأنها باعتبار الحاجة في حقهم وفي حق المرأة معاوضة عن الاحتباس، ولهذا إذا ضاعت النفقة أو الكسوة من أيديهم يفرض لهم أخرى لما ذكرنا ا وقد استفيد من هذه المنقولات
In al-Dhakhira: If the judge fixed clothing for her and it is lost, stolen, or torn before the time, then he does not have to give her clothing until the time when the clothing would not survive passes. The principle is that if the judge's error in estimation becomes apparent, he returns it; if not, he does not. If the clothing is torn by use before the time, consideration is given: if torn by misuse, the error in estimation is not evident, so no other clothing is given until that time passes; if torn by normal use, the error is evident, so another clothing is given. The same answer for maintenance if it is lost, stolen, eaten, wasted or not, and that is before the time, it is as we said for clothing. If the period passes and the clothing remains, if it was not used at all until the time passed, the judge fixes another clothing because no error is evident. If it was used, and it was used along with another clothing in that period, the judge fixes another clothing in that period. If it was not used with another clothing, no other clothing is fixed because his error became apparent: he set a time after which the clothing would still survive. There is a difference between this and when the judge fixes ten dirhams for monthly maintenance and the month passes and something remains of the ten: he fixes another ten. The difference is that in maintenance, the judge's error is not certain; perhaps she stinted on spending, so the estimation remains valid. In clothing, if she wore it the entire period without tearing, then his error is certain – we are sure she did not stint in wearing. There is also a difference between maintenance and clothing for wives and for relatives. For relatives, if the time passes and something remains of the money or clothing, the judge does not fix another in any case because it is based on need for them. For the wife, it is compensation for her confinement. Therefore, if the maintenance or clothing is lost from their hands, another is fixed for them, due to what we mentioned. This is what is learned from these quotations.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage from al-Dhakhira details the consequences after the judge has fixed clothing or maintenance. If the clothing is lost or destroyed before the period, the husband does not have to replace it until the period ends, unless the destruction was due to normal wear, indicating the judge underestimated the need. Similarly for maintenance money left over: the judge continues to give the same amount because the leftover may be due to her thrift. For clothing, if it remains intact after the period, the judge's estimation was too generous, so no new clothing is given. There is also a distinction between spouses and relatives: for relatives, no new provision is given because it is based on need, while for the wife it is compensation for her confinement. Therefore, if the maintenance or clothing is lost from relatives, another is fixed for them because they are needy, unlike the wife's case where it is compensation.

Key Terms
التخرق (al-takharruq): Tearing or wearing out of clothing; the manner of tearing (misuse vs. normal use) determines if the judge's estimation was wrong.
التقتير (al-taqtir): Stinting or being overly frugal; if a wife spends less on maintenance or uses clothing sparingly, the judge's estimation remains valid.
الخطأ في التقدير (al-khata' fi al-taqdir): Error in judicial estimation; if the clothing lasts beyond the period without wearing out, the judge's estimation is shown to be too generous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband must give new clothing
B) The judge's estimation is proven correct and no new clothing is given
C) The wife can demand new clothing immediately
D) The husband is excused from providing any clothing in the future

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the continued validity of a judge's estimation depends on whether subsequent events prove it erroneous; misuse does not trigger replacement, while normal wear does for clothing, but leftover maintenance money does not alone indicate error.

Husband's Obligation to Provide Bedding and Clothing for His Wife
Expands on the obligation of kiswah and firash with detailed rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the husband's obligation to provide separate bedding and clothing, and apply the rules for when leftover items require new provision.

Core Idea
Kiswah and firash are wajib; leftover items after the term do not reduce the husband's future obligation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the husband's duty to provide his wife with separate bedding and clothing as part of nafaqah. It also addresses an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the standard for clothing considers only the husband's status or both spouses' statuses. Additionally, it provides nuanced rules for when clothing is destroyed or remains after the prescribed term, distinguishing between wives and relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the husband is obligated to provide: separate bedding (mattress, pillow, blanket) and clothing (dir' or qamis). The ruling is wajib as part of nafaqah.
Separate bedding is required due to potential isolation during menstruation or illness.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the disagreement: al-Khassaf considers both spouses' statuses for kiswah, while others consider only the husband's status. Both views are presented.
The source of the different views is al-Bada'i'.
3
Analyze the ruling on loss or wear of kiswah
If kiswah is destroyed or worn before the term, the husband does not replace it unless the judge's estimation error becomes apparent (e.g., normal wear indicates overestimation).
Misuse does not show error; normal wear does.
4
Distinguish between kiswah and nafaqah
Leftover money from nafaqah may be due to economizing, so the obligation continues; leftover intac...
The distinction is based on the possibility of economizing in nafaqah but not in kiswah wearing.
5
Contrast wives with relatives
For relatives, leftover resources terminate the obligation because it is need-based; for wives, it is a compensation for seclusion (ihtibas), so the obligation persists.
This distinction is the effective cause (illa) for the different rulings.

حدة ولم يكتف بفراش واحد لأنها ربما تعتزل عنه في أيام الحيض أو في زمان مرضها ا وفي فتح القدير : ذكر في الأصل الدرع من الكسوة والخصاف ذكر القميص وهما سواء إلا أن القميص يكون مجيباً من قبل الكتف والدرع من قبل الصدر. هـ. وفي البدائع الكسوة على الاختلاف كالنفقة من اعتبار حاله فقط أو حالهما على قول الخصاف. وفي الذخيرة : إذا فرض لها القاضي الكسوة فهلكت أو سرقت منها أو خرقتها قبل الوقت فليس عليه أن يكسوها حتى يمضي الوقت الذي لا تبقى إليه الكسوة. والأصل أن القاضي متى ظهر له الخطأ في التقدير يرده فإذا لم يظهر له ذلك لا يرده، فإن تخرقت الكسوة بالاستعمال قبل مضي الوقت ينظر ؛ فإن تخرقت بخرق استعمالها لم يتبين الخطأ في التقدير فلا يقضي بكسوة أخرى ما لم يمض ذلك الوقت، وإن تخرقت بالاستعمال المعتاد تبين الخطأ في التقدير فيقضي بكسوة أخرى، وكذا الجواب في النفقة إذا ضاعت أو سرقت أو أكلت أو أسرفت أو لم تسرف وكان ذلك قبل مضي الوقت فهو كما قلنا في الكسوة، ولو مضت المدة والكسوة باقية فإن لم تستعمل تلك الكسوة أصلاً حتى مضى الوقت يفرض القاضي لها كسوة أخرى لأنه لم يظهر خطأ القاضي في التقدير، وإن استعملت تلك الكسوة، فإن استعملت معها كسوة أخرى في تلك المدة يفرض لها القاضي كسوة أخرى في تلك المدة، وإن لم تستعمل مع هذه الكسوة كسوة أخرى لا يفرض لها أخرى لأنه ظهر خطؤه في التقدير حيث وقت وقتاً تبقى الكسوة وراء ذلك الوقت. فرق بين وبين ما إذا فرض لها القاضي عشرة دراهم نفقة شهر فمضى الشهر وقد بقي من العشرة شيء حيث يفرض لها القاضي في النفقة عشرة أخرى، والفرق أن في باب النفقة لم يظهر خطأ القاضي في التقدير بيقين الجواز أنه إنما بقي من العشرة شيء لتقتير وجد منها في الإنفاق على نفسها فبقي التقدير معتبراً فيقضي القاضي لها بعشرة أخرى، أما في باب الكسوة إذا لبست جميع المدة ولم تتخرق فقد ظهر خطأ القاضي في التقدير بيقين لأنا تيقنا أنه لم يوجد منها التقتير في اللبس. فرق بين نفقة الزوجات وكسوتهن وبين نفقة المحارم وكسوتهم فإن في الأقارب إذا مضى الوقت وبقي شيء من الدراهم أو الكسوة فإن القاضي لا يقضي بأخرى في الأحوال كلها لأنها باعتبار الحاجة في حقهم وفي حق المرأة معاوضة عن الاحتباس، ولهذا إذا ضاعت النفقة أو الكسوة من أيديهم يفرض لهم أخرى لما ذكرنا ا وقد استفيد من هذه المنقولات
The passage of time is a condition, and the husband may bring her to the judge so that he orders her to wear the garment because adornment is his right. This indicates that if the woman withholds the nafaqah and eats little and economizes on herself, he may bring her to the judge so that she eats what is prescribed for her, for fear of emaciation harming him. In Ghayat al-Bayan, attributed to al-Khassaf: 'He should provide for her what she sleeps on, such as a mattress, pillow, and rug in winter, and a blanket to cover herself.' Shams al-A'imma said in Sharh Kitab al-Nafaqat: 'He mentioned for her a separate bed and was not satisfied with one bed because she may isolate herself from him during menstruation or illness.' In Fath al-Qadir: 'In al-Asl, the dir' is mentioned for clothing, and al-Khassaf mentioned the qamis, and they are the same, except that the qamis is opened from the shoulder and the dir' from the chest.' End. In al-Bada'i': 'Kiswah, on the differing view, is like nafaqah: whether considering only his status or both their statuses, according to al-Khassaf's statement.' In al-Dhakhirah: 'If the judge prescribes for her the kiswah, and it is destroyed, stolen, or torn before the term, he is not required to clothe her until the term after which the kiswah does not survive passes. The principle is: whenever the error in estimation becomes apparent to the judge, he revokes it; if it does not become apparent, he does not revoke it. If the kiswah wears out from use before the term passes, it is considered: if it wears out due to misuse, the error in estimation is not apparent, so he does not order another kiswah until that term passes. If it wears out from normal use, the error in estimation becomes apparent, so he orders another kiswah. Similarly, the answer for nafaqah: if it is lost, stolen, consumed, wasted, or not wasted, before the term passes, it is as we said for kiswah. If the term passes and the kiswah remains, if that kiswah was never used at all until the term passed, the judge prescribes another kiswah because the judge's error in estimation is not apparent. If she used that kiswah, then if she used another kiswah along with it during that term, the judge prescribes another kiswah for that term. If she did not use another kiswah with this one, he does not prescribe another because his error in estimation became apparent, since he set a term after which the kiswah still survives. There is a distinction between this and the case where the judge prescribed ten dirhams as nafaqah for a month, and the month passes with some of the ten remaining, where the judge prescribes another ten for nafaqah. The difference is that in the chapter of nafaqah, the judge's error in estimation does not become apparent with certainty because the remainder may be due to the wife's economizing on herself, so the estimation remains valid, and the judge prescribes another ten. In the chapter of kiswah, if she wore it for the entire term and it did not wear out, the judge's error in estimation becomes apparent with certainty, for we are certain that she did not economize in wearing. There is a distinction between the nafaqah and kiswah of wives and the nafaqah and kiswah of close relatives. For relatives, if the term passes and something of the dirhams or kiswah remains, the judge does not prescribe another in all cases, because it is based on need for them, whereas for the woman, it is a compensation for her seclusion. Hence, if the nafaqah or kiswah is lost from their hands, he prescribes another for them, as we mentioned. And from these transmitted rulings, benefits are derived.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling-with-proof about the husband's obligation to provide bedding and clothing for his wife, and the legal consequences when items are destroyed or remain after the prescribed term. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq first mentions that the husband can ask the judge to order the wife to wear proper attire, since her adornment is his right. This implies that if she withholds from eating to save money, he may intervene to prevent harm. Al-Khassaf is quoted stating that the wife must be given separate bedding (mattress, pillow, rug in winter, and blanket) because she may need to sleep separately during menstruation or illness. A dispute is noted regarding clothing: in al-Asl, the garment is a 'dir'' (opening from chest), while al-Khassaf mentions a 'qamis' (opening from shoulder), but both are equivalent. Another intra-Hanafi disagreement is cited from al-Bada'i': whether the standard for kiswah considers only the husband's status or both spouses' statuses, with al-Khassaf holding the latter. The passage then explains principles for when kiswah is lost or worn out. If the clothing is destroyed before the term ends, the husband need not replace it until the term expires, assuming the judge's estimation was correct. However, if it wears out from normal use, the judge's error is shown, and he must order new clothing. For nafaqah money saved by the wife, the judge continues the same amount because economizing is possible, but for clothing that is not worn out, the estimation is clearly wrong. A key distinction is made between wives and relatives: for relatives, leftover resources terminate the obligation because it is based on need, while for wives it is a contractual exchange for seclusion (ihtibas). This distinction is the 'illa (effective cause) for the different rulings.

Key Terms
الكسوة (al-kiswah): Clothing that the husband must provide for his wife, including garments like dir' (chemise) and qamis (shirt), as well as bedding.
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance including food, clothing, and shelter that a husband must provide for his wife in exchange for her seclusion (ihtibas).
الفراش (al-firash): Bedding including mattress, pillow, and blanket, which the husband must provide separately for the wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, if the wife's clothing is destroyed before the term ends due to her misuse, what is the ruling?
A) The husband must replace it immediately.
B) The husband does not replace it until the term expires.
C) The judge orders a new garment at his discretion.
D) The wife must pay for the replacement.

Key Takeaway
Kiswah and firash are wajib obligations with distinct rules: leftover items do not reduce future obligations due to the nature of ihtibas, and the standard for provision may consider both spouses' statuses.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate

Derived Rulings on Wife's Maintenance
Summarizes derived rulings from earlier transmitted rulings regarding the wife's maintenance needs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four derived rulings regarding the wife's maintenance and explain why the husband's obligation remains even if the wife owns her own goods.

Core Idea
Wife's own property does not negate husband's duty to provide separate necessities.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq gathers several practical conclusions (mustafidat) from earlier transmitted rulings on maintenance (nafaqah). These rulings clarify the husband's absolute obligation to provide clothing, bedding, and household items, and they emphasize that the wife's personal wealth does not reduce this duty. The author also addresses savings, household utensils, and the husband's responsibility to purchase goods. We will unpack each point to understand the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
Recognize that the husband must provide all necessary clothing and bedding for the wife, either directly or through a court order every six months.
The judge can prescribe items or a monetary equivalent.
2
Understand the purchase responsibility
Normally the husband should purchase the goods, but if he delays or is treacherous, the wife may do it herself or appoint an agent.
This protects the wife from neglect.
3
Apply the principle of non-offsetting
Even if the wife already owns her own bedding or clothing, the husband must still provide; she is not required to use her own property, a fortiori not to provide for him.
This distinguishes her property from the husband's obligation.
4
Recognize the wife's savings
If the husband gives her maintenance and she saves part of it, those savings belong to her; he cannot take them back.
The wife is not required to spend her own money on household needs.
5
Identify household utensils and concluding principle
Utensils are on the husband. The overarching principle: the wife's only duty is to submit herself in his house; he must provide all necessities according to their status.
Forcing the wife to use her own goods is haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد استفيد من هذه المنقولات أشياء منها : أن جميع ما تحتاج إليه المرأة من لباس بدنها وفرش بيتها مما تنام عليه وتتغطى به فإنه لازم على الرجل ؛ إما أن يأتي به، وإما إن يفرضه القاضي عليه أصنافاً أو دراهم كل ستة أشهر ويعجلها لها. وينبغي أن يلي الزوج شراء الأمتعة لها كما قدمناه في الإنفاق إلا إذا ظهر مطله أو خيانته في الشراء لها فحينئذ هي التي تلي ذلك بنفسها أو بوكيلها. ومنها أنها لو كان لها أمتعه من فرش ونحوها لا يسقط عن الزوج ذلك بل يجب لها عليه ما ذكرناه، وإن كان لها أمتعه فلا يلزمها أن تلبس متاعها ولا أن تنام على فراشها فبالأولى أن لا يلزمها أن تفرش متاعها لينام عليه أو يجلس عليه ومنها أنه إذا دفع لها نفقتها وأنفقت منها قليلاً وأمسكت الباقي فإن لها ذلك كما قدمناه ومنها أن أدوات البيت كالأواني ونحوها على الرجل. والحاصل أن المرأة ليس لها إلا تسليم نفسها في بيته، وعليه لها جميع ما يكفيها بحسب حالهما من أكل وشرب ولبس وفرش ولا يلزمها أن تستمتع بما هو ملكها ولا أن تفرش له شيئاً من فراشها. وإنما أكثرنا من هذه المسائل تنبيهاً للأزواج لما نراه في زماننا من تقصيرهم في حقوقهن حتى إنه يأمرها بفرش أمتعتها جبراً عليها وكذلك لأضيافه، وبعضم لا يعطي لها كسوة حتى كانت عند الدخول غنية صارت فقيرة وهذا كله حرام لا يجوز نعوذ بالله من شرور أنفسنا ومن سيئات أعمالنا
From these transmitted rulings, several things are derived: (1) All that the woman needs for her body's clothing and the bedding of her house, such as what she sleeps on and covers herself with, is obligatory upon the man. Either he provides it, or the judge prescribes it for him in categories or dirhams every six months and gives it to her promptly. The husband should undertake the purchase of the goods for her, as we presented regarding spending, except if his delay or treachery in purchasing for her becomes apparent; then she undertakes that herself or through her agent. (2) If she already has goods such as bedding and the like, that does not relieve the husband; rather, what we mentioned is obligatory for him. If she has goods, she is not obligated to wear her own goods nor to sleep on her own bedding; a fortiori, she is not obligated to spread her goods for him to sleep or sit on. (3) If he gives her her nafaqah and she spends a little and keeps the rest, that belongs to her, as we presented. (4) Household utensils such as vessels and the like are upon the husband. The conclusion is that the woman only has to submit herself in his house, and he must provide for her all that suffices her according to their status, in food, drink, clothing, and bedding. She is not obligated to benefit from what is her property, nor to spread any of her bedding for him. We have elaborated on these issues to alert husbands, because of what we see in our time of their negligence in her rights, so much so that he forces her to spread her goods for him and for his guests, and some do not give her clothing so that she, who was wealthy at the time of marriage, becomes poor. All of this is forbidden, not permissible. We seek refuge with Allah from the evils of our souls and from our evil deeds.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a list of derived rulings (mustafidat) from the earlier transmitted rulings (manqulat). The author presents them as practical conclusions for husbands. First, all clothing and bedding needs of the wife are obligatory on the husband, either provided directly or through court order every six months. The husband should do the purchasing, but if he delays or is dishonest, the wife may do it herself or appoint an agent. Second, even if the wife owns her own bedding or clothing, this does not relieve the husband; she is not required to use her own property. The phrase 'a fortiori' (bil-awla) means that if she is not forced to wear her own clothes, even more so she need not provide bedding for him. Third, if the husband gives her nafaqah and she saves some, that saving is hers; she is not obligated to spend on him. Fourth, household utensils (e.g., pots, pans) are the husband's responsibility. The author emphasizes that the wife's only duty is to submit herself in his house; he must provide all necessities according to their mutual status. The passage ends with a strong admonition against contemporary husbands who force wives to use their own goods or fail to provide clothing, deeming such behavior haram.

Key Terms
الأمتعة (al-amti'ah): Goods such as bedding, clothing, and household items that the wife may own. The husband must still provide separate items.
الأواني (al-awani): Household vessels and utensils, which are the husband's responsibility to provide.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the derived rulings, if the husband gives his wife her nafaqah and she saves some of it, what is the ruling on those savings?
A) The husband can take them back.
B) They belong to the wife.
C) They must be spent on household items.
D) The judge decides their disposition.

Key Takeaway
A wife's personal belongings do not relieve the husband of his duty to provide separate necessities.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Who Is Entitled to Nafaqah? The Wife in a Valid Marriage
Defines the wife entitled to nafaqah and illustrates with cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which women are entitled to nafaqah and apply the rule that nafaqah is only for a wife in a valid (sahih) marriage.

Core Idea
Nafaqah is only for a wife in a valid marriage; a fasid marriage or proven impediment revokes all nafaqah.

This passage clarifies a crucial condition for nafaqah: only a wife in a valid (sahih) marriage is entitled to financial support. It also addresses what happens when the marriage is later found to be invalid, such as in cases of fosterage or conflicting claims. Understanding this definition prevents misapplication of nafaqah rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term: 'wife' in the context of nafaqah
The author specifies that the wife entitled to nafaqah is the one in reality (fi nafs al-amr) through a valid marriage. Distinguish between apparent and actual marital status.
Underline 'في نفس الأمر' (in reality) — this is the criterion.
2
Determine the ruling for a fasid marriage
The text explicitly denies nafaqah for a wife in a fasid (defective) marriage, both before and after separation. Understand that fasid marriage does not create the obligations that nafaqah compensates.
Fasid includes marriages without witnesses or with temporary impediments.
3
Analyze the foster sister case
If a woman receives nafaqah but later it is proven she is a foster sister (permanent impediment), the marriage is invalid ab initio, and all nafaqah must be returned.
This shows nafaqah is tied to the validity of the marriage itself.
4
Consider the case of conflicting claims (two sisters)
When two women each claim to be the wife, and the husband denies, but both produce evidence of marriage and cohabitation, the text rules that each gets the nafaqah of one woman (half) during investigation. This highlights that nafaqah is allocated based on evidence of a valid marriage.
The ruling is from al-Khassaf – it is a practical solution for uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بالزوجة في قوله «تجب للزوجة» الزوجة في نفس الأمر بنكاح صحيح لأنه لا نفقة للزوجة بنكاح فاسد لا قبل التفريق ولا بعده، ولا نفقة للزوجة ظاهراً إلا في نفس الأمر ولهذا قال في الظهيرية لو أن امرأة أخذت نفقتها من زوجها أشهراً ثم شهد شاهدان أنها أخته من الرضاع يفرق بينهما ويرجع عليها الزوج بما أخذت. وذكر قبله : أختان ادعت كل واحدة منهما أن هذا زوجها وهو يجحد فأقامتا البينة على النكاح والدخول فلهما نفقة امرأة واحدة في مدة المسألة عن الشهود؛ نص عليه الخصاف
And by 'wife' in his statement 'nafaqah is obligatory for the wife' is meant the wife in reality, through a valid (sahih) marriage, because there is no nafaqah for a wife in a fasid (defective) marriage, neither before separation nor after. And there is no nafaqah for a wife outwardly except in reality. Hence, it is said in al-Zahiriyyah: If a woman took her nafaqah from her husband for months, then two witnesses testified that she was his foster sister, they are separated, and the husband recovers from her what she took. And mentioned before it: Two sisters, each claiming that this man is her husband while he denies, and they both produce evidence of marriage and cohabitation, then they each have the nafaqah of one woman during the questioning period of the witnesses; this is stated by al-Khassaf.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage defines who exactly is meant by 'wife' in the context of obligatory nafaqah. The author clarifies that it refers to a wife in reality (fi nafs al-amr) through a valid (sahih) marriage. A woman in a fasid (defective) marriage, such as one lacking a proper witness or with a temporary condition, is not entitled to nafaqah either before or after separation. Additionally, if it later becomes clear that the woman was actually a mahram (e.g., foster sister), she must return all nafaqah received. The passage also cites a case from al-Khassaf: two sisters both claim to be married to the same man, who denies both. They produce evidence of marriage and cohabitation. While the witnesses are being questioned, each gets the nafaqah of one woman (i.e., half the normal amount), because the truth is uncertain. This shows that nafaqah is tied to actual marital status.

Key Terms
النكاح الصحيح (al-nikah al-sahih): A marriage that fulfills all conditions and pillars of validity, as opposed to a fasid (defective) marriage.
النكاح الفاسد (al-nikah al-fasid): A marriage with a defect in its conditions, such as marriage without witnesses, or during 'iddah, or with a mahram. It is invalid and does not confer nafaqah.
الرضاع (al-rada'): Fosterage; a woman who was breastfed by the same woman as the husband becomes his foster sister, making the marriage invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for nafaqah to be obligatory?
A) The wife must be in a valid (sahih) marriage.
B) The wife must be living with the husband.
C) The wife must have children with the husband.
D) The wife must have a written marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
Nafaqah is a right that only arises from a valid (sahih) marriage; if the marriage is later found invalid, all nafaqah must be returned.

Nafaqah When Wife Withholds for Mahr: Imam vs Sahibayn
Explains nafaqah obligation when wife withholds for mahr; intra-Hanafi dispute on minors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling of nafaqah when a wife withholds for the prompt mahr and distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding minors.

Core Idea
Nafaqah remains wajib even if wife withholds for mahr; Sahibayn exempt minors because father's delivery is invalid.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the wife's right to nafaqah when she withholds herself due to non-payment of the prompt mahr. While Imam Abu Hanifa holds that nafaqah is still obligatory, the two Sahibayn make an exception for minor wives. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists balance rights and obligations in marriage.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, nafaqah is wajib even if the wife withholds for the prompt mahr.
The reason: the husband caused the forfeiture of seclusion by not paying mahr.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's exception
The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no nafaqah if the wife is below puberty because the father's delivery is invalid.
This exception is limited to minors.
3
Analyze the proof of each
Imam's proof: the husband's failure to pay mahr makes the withholding justified. Sahibayn's proof: a minor cannot validly be delivered by the father.
Text: 'لعدم صحة تسليم الأب'
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
For an adult wife, all agree nafaqah is due. For a minor wife, Sahibayn deny nafaqah; Imam affirms.
This is the practical difference.
5
Consider the tarjih
Later scholars rely on Imam's view as more general; the Sahibayn's exception is confined to the minor case.
The author of al-Bahr implicitly prefers Imam's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو مانعة نفسها للمهر) أي يجب عليه النفقة ولو كانت المرأة مانعة نفسها بحق كالمنع القبض مهرها. والمراد منه المعجل إما نصاً أو عرفاً كما أسلفناه لأنه فوت الاحتباس لمعنى من قبله فيجعل كلا فائت أطلقه فشمل المنع بعد الدخول وهو قول الإمام. وقالا : لا نفقة لها إذا كانت دون البلوغ لعدم صحة تسليم الأب وقد قدمناه. قيدنا قوله : (فبالأولى أن لا يلزمها أن تفرش متاعها الخ قال في النهر : لكن قدمنا عنه في باب المهر معزياً إلى المبتغى أنها لو زفت إليه بلا جهاز يليق به فله مطالبة الأب بما دفعه من الدراهم والدنانير إلا إذا سكت ا هـ . وعلى هذا فإذا زفت إليه به لا يحرم علية الانتفاع به، وفي عرفنا يلتزمون كثرة المهر لكثرة الجهاز وقلته لقلته، ولا شك أن المعروف كالمشروط فينبغي العمل بما مر وقال بعض الفضلاء قال الحموي بعد نقله : وفيه نظر لأن ما في المبتغى ضعيف كما اعترف به هو في باب المهر والعرف إنما يعمل به إذا كان عاماً فالحق ما في البحر ا هـ قوله : (وأراد بالزوجة اه.
His statement: 'Even if she withholds herself for the mahr' means that nafaqah is obligatory upon him even if the woman withholds herself by right, such as withholding for the receipt of her mahr. And what is meant by it is the prompt (mu'ajjal) mahr, either by textual stipulation or custom, as we have stated before, because she forfeits (fawt) the seclusion (ihtibas) due to a reason from his side, so it is treated as if both are forfeited. This is general, so it includes withholding after cohabitation, and this is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: No nafaqah for her if she is below the age of puberty, because the father's delivery is not valid, and we have already presented that. We have qualified his statement: 'a fortiori, she is not obligated to spread her goods...' In al-Nahr it is said: 'But we have previously quoted from al-Mubtagha, attributed to al-Mubtagha, that if she is handed over to him without a suitable dowry (jihaz), he may demand from her father what he paid of dirhams and dinars, unless he remained silent.' End. Upon this, if she is handed over with it, it is not forbidden for him to benefit from it. In our custom, they undertake a large mahr for a large dowry and small for small, no doubt that the known (al-ma'ruf) is like the stipulated, so it is appropriate to act according to what has passed. Some virtuous people said: Al-Hamawi said after quoting it: 'There is consideration in it, because what is in al-Mubtagha is weak, as he himself admitted in the chapter of mahr, and custom is only acted upon if it is general. So the correct is what is in al-Bahr.' End. His statement: 'And by wife he meant...'
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wife's nafaqah when she withholds herself (tamanna') due to non-payment of the prompt mahr (mu'ajjal). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that nafaqah is still obligatory because the reason for forfeiting seclusion (ihtibas) is from the husband's side (failure to pay mahr), so the wife's right to nafaqah remains. This applies even if the withholding occurs after cohabitation. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree when the wife is a minor (below puberty), because her father's delivery of her is invalid, so she is not considered truly 'withholding' by right. The author then moves to a related issue about dowry (jihaz). He quotes from al-Nahr that if a wife is handed over to her husband without a suitable dowry, the husband can demand from her father what he paid (in mahr) unless he consented. This implies that the husband may use the dowry if it is provided. The author notes that in their custom, the mahr is tied to the dowry amount, so this should be considered. However, al-Hamawi criticizes the reliance on al-Mubtagha as weak and says the correct view is in al-Bahr (the author's own work). The author ends by repeating the opening phrase about the definition of wife, which is cut off.

Key Terms
مانعة نفسها (mani'atu nafsiha): A wife who withholds herself from her husband, refusing to allow him sexual access, for a valid reason such as unpaid prompt mahr.
المهر المعجل (al-mahr al-mu'ajjal): The prompt portion of the mahr that is due immediately upon marriage, as opposed to the deferred portion (mu'ajjal).
الجهاز (al-jihaz): Dowry or household items that the wife brings into the marriage from her family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nafaqah is suspended until she submits.
B) Nafaqah is still obligatory.
C) Nafaqah is forfeited permanently.
D) Nafaqah is reduced by half.

Key Takeaway
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, a wife does not forfeit her right to nafaqah by withholding for the prompt mahr; only Sahibayn make an exception for minors due to invalid father delivery.

Components of Maintenance (Nafaqah) in the Hanafi School
Listing the components of maintenance and warning husbands against neglect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the components of maintenance (nafaqah) that a husband must provide for his wife according to the Hanafi school, and explain why the wife's own property does not exempt him.

Core Idea
Maintenance is the husband's duty even if the wife is wealthy — her property is her own, not a substitute.

The husband's obligation to provide maintenance (nafaqah) is a core right of the wife in Islamic law. This lesson, drawn from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, details exactly what the husband must supply: clothing, bedding, and household utensils. It also clarifies that the wife's own furniture does not relieve the husband, and warns against common neglect. By the end, you will be able to identify these obligations and understand their binding nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hukm and Its Authority
Determine the legal ruling (wajib) and note that the text uses 'lazim' (obligatory). The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, indicating strong authority.
Wajib here means binding; failure is sinful and enforceable by a judge.
2
List the Components of Maintenance
Extract the specific items mentioned: clothing for the body, bedding (mattress, covers), and household utensils (pots, etc.). These are the core necessities.
The text also mentions food and drink as part of the general obligation.
3
Understand Key Clarifications
Note two key clarifications: (a) the wife's own property does not exempt the husband, and (b) if the husband pays and the wife saves some, it is hers to keep.
The principle: the wife is not obliged to use her own wealth for household needs.
4
Apply the Admonition
Recognize that the author's warning against neglect elevated the ruling to a serious matter (haram). This reinforces the importance of fulfilling these duties.
Contemporary relevance: many husbands fall short; this text serves as a clear reminder.

Source Text

Among the things: that all that the woman needs of clothing for her body and bedding for her house, on which she sleeps and covers herself, is obligatory upon the man; either he brings it, or the judge imposes it upon him in kinds or dirhams every six months and pays it promptly to her. And it is appropriate that the husband undertake the purchase of the goods for her, as we have previously mentioned in the chapter on spending, unless his delay or deception in purchasing for her appears; then it is she who undertakes that herself or through her agent. And among them: that if she has goods such as bedding and the like, it does not fall from the husband; rather, what we have mentioned is obligatory for her; and if she has goods, she is not obliged to wear her own clothing nor to sleep on her own bedding; so a fortiori she is not obliged to spread her goods for him to sleep or sit on. And among them: that if he pays her her maintenance and she spends a little from it and keeps the rest, then that is hers, as we have previously mentioned. And among them: that the household utensils such as pots and the like are upon the man. The conclusion is that the woman has nothing but to submit herself in his house, and upon him is all that suffices her according to their condition, of food, drink, clothing, and bedding; and she is not obliged to enjoy what is her property, nor to spread for him anything from her bedding. And we have elaborated on these issues to alert husbands because of what we see in our time of their shortcomings in their rights, to the extent that he orders her to spread her goods coercively, and likewise for his guests; and some do not give her clothing, so that she, who upon entering was rich, becomes poor; all of this is forbidden, not permissible; we seek refuge with Allah from the evils of ourselves and from the evil of our deeds.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the husband's maintenance obligations. The author lists items such as clothing, bedding, and household utensils, emphasizing that these are mandatory (لازم). The husband must either provide them himself or the judge can enforce it. The wife is not required to use her own property for these needs; the husband remains obligated even if she has her own belongings. If the husband pays maintenance and the wife saves some, it is hers. The passage concludes with a strong admonition against husbands who neglect these duties, declaring such behavior as haram. This is based on standard Hanafi rulings from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance that the husband is obliged to provide for his wife, including food, clothing, and housing.

D) Only the prompt dower

Key Takeaway
The husband's obligation to provide maintenance is independent of the wife's wealth; he must provide clothing, bedding, utensils, and all basic needs.

Maintenance Only in Valid Marriage
Defining that maintenance is only obligatory in a valid marriage and not in a fasid marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that maintenance (nafaqah) is obligatory only in a valid marriage (nikah sahih) and explain that no maintenance is due in a fasid marriage, applying the illustrative cases from the text.

Core Idea
Maintenance is only owed in a valid marriage; a defective (fasid) marriage does not obligate nafaqah.

This lesson clarifies a key principle in Hanafi family law: maintenance (nafaqah) is tied to the reality of a valid marriage, not mere appearance. The text from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the term 'wife' in the context of maintenance means a wife in a valid nikah. Therefore, if a marriage is fasid (defective), no maintenance is due, even if the marriage appears valid. Two illustrative cases reinforce this: a woman who took maintenance but was later found to be a foster-sister must repay, and two sisters both claiming the same husband share half maintenance during their dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the first sentence: maintenance is only for a wife in a valid marriage. Note that the author explicitly excludes fasid marriage.
The ruling is straightforward: no nafaqah in fasid nikah.
2
Analyze the illustrative cases
Examine the two scenarios: (1) a woman who later is proven a foster-sister must return maintenance; (2) two sisters each claiming the same husband get half maintenance during the dispute. Both show that maintenance is based on the reality of the marriage, not appearance.
The second case is unique: because neither can prove exclusive right, they share half the maintenance.
3
Extract the underlying principle
The principle is that maintenance is a right arising from a valid marriage contract. A fasid contract does not create this right because the woman is not legally bound (ihtibas) to the husband.
This principle is consistent across Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد بالزوجة في قوله «تجب للزوجة» الزوجة في نفس الأمر بنكاح صحيح لأنه لا نفقة للزوجة بنكاح فاسد لا قبل التفريق ولا بعده، ولا نفقة للزوجة ظاهراً إلا في نفس الأمر ولهذا قال في الظهيرية لو أن امرأة أخذت نفقتها من زوجها أشهراً ثم شهد شاهدان أنها أخته من الرضاع يفرق بينهما ويرجع عليها الزوج بما أخذت. وذكر قبله : أختان ادعت كل واحدة منهما أن هذا زوجها وهو يجحد فأقامتا البينة على النكاح والدخول فلهما نفقة امرأة واحدة في مدة المسألة عن الشهود؛ نص عليه الخصاف.
And he meant by 'wife' in his statement 'maintenance is obligatory for the wife' the wife in reality in a valid marriage, because there is no maintenance for a wife in a fasid marriage, neither before separation nor after it; and there is no maintenance for a wife apparently except in reality. That is why he said in al-Zahiriyyah: if a woman took her maintenance from her husband for months, then two witnesses testified that she is his foster-sister, they are separated and the husband recovers from her what she took. And it was mentioned before him: two sisters, each claiming that this is her husband while he denies, and they established evidence of marriage and consummation; then they have the maintenance of one woman for the duration of the case regarding the witnesses; al-Khassaf explicitly stated it.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling clarifying the term 'wife' in the context of maintenance. The author explains that maintenance is only obligatory in a valid marriage (نكاح صحيح). In a fasid marriage (defective in essence), no maintenance is due before or after separation. Even if the marriage appears valid (e.g., witnesses later proven false), maintenance is not genuinely owed. Two illustrative cases are given: a woman who took maintenance but was later found to be a foster-sister must repay; two sisters claiming the same husband each get half maintenance during dispute. This reinforces that maintenance is tied to the reality of a valid marriage, not mere appearance.

Key Terms
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): A marriage contract that is invalid due to a deficiency such as lack of witnesses or a permanent impediment.
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, owed by the husband to the wife in a valid marriage.
نكاح صحيح (nikah sahih): A valid marriage contract fulfilling all conditions and free from defects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Maintenance is only compulsory in a valid marriage; a fasid marriage does not create any nafaqah obligation, and any maintenance taken must be returned if the marriage is proven invalid.

Maintenance for a Wife Preventing Herself for Prompt Dower
Intra-Hanafi dispute on maintenance for a wife preventing herself for prompt dower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on maintenance when a wife prevents herself for prompt dower and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A wife's prevention for prompt dower is a right, so maintenance remains due even after consummation according to the fatwa.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh: does a woman forfeit her maintenance if she withholds herself from her husband until she receives her prompt dower? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differed on this point, especially when the wife is a minor. Understanding this dispute reveals how the school weighs competing principles: the wife's right to ihtibas (detention) versus the husband's obligation to provide maintenance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: the wife prevents herself from submission to receive her prompt dower. The ruling under dispute: is maintenance (nafaqah) wajib upon the husband?
The baseline: if the prevention is by right (bi haqq), it is not nushuz.
2
State the Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa: maintenance wajib in all cases, including after consummation and for a minor. Sahibayn: no maintenance if the wife is a minor because the father's submission is invalid.
Both agree that if the dower is entirely deferred, prevention is nushuz and no maintenance.
3
Analyze the proof structure
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas: she forfeits ihtibas for a reason from the husband's side, so it is as if she did not forfeit. Sahibayn restrict this to non-minors because the father cannot validly submit the minor wife.
The text 'فهو كلا فائت' captures the analogy.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view that she has the right to prevent, thus maintenance is due. This is the operative ruling.
The text explicitly states 'الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو مانعة نفسها للمهر) أي يجب عليه النفقة ولو كانت المرأة مانعة نفسها بحق كالمنع القبض مهرها. والمراد منه المعجل إما نصاً أو عرفاً كما أسلفناه لأنه فوت الاحتباس لمعنى من قبله فيجعل كلا فائت أطلقه فشمل المنع بعد الدخول وهو قول الإمام. وقالا : لا نفقة لها إذا كانت دون البلوغ لعدم صحة تسليم الأب وقد قدمناه. قيدنا قوله : (فبالأولى أن لا يلزمها أن تفرش متاعها الخ قال في النهر : لكن قدمنا عنه في باب المهر معزياً إلى المبتغى أنها لو زفت إليه بلا جهاز يليق به فله مطالبة الأب بما دفعه من الدراهم والدنانير إلا إذا سكت ا هـ . وعلى هذا فإذا زفت إليه به لا يحرم علية الانتفاع به، وفي عرفنا يلتزمون كثرة المهر لكثرة الجهاز وقلته لقلته، ولا شك أن المعروف كالمشروط فينبغي العمل بما مر وقال بعض الفضلاء قال الحموي بعد نقله : وفيه نظر لأن ما في المبتغى ضعيف كما اعترف به هو في باب المهر والعرف إنما يعمل به إذا كان عاماً فالحق ما في البحر ا هـ قوله : (وأراد بالزوجة اه. بالمعجل لأنه لو كان كله مؤجلاً فامتنعت فلا نفقة لها لأنه نشوز كما في غاية البيان، وقدمنا أن الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف من أن لها المنع فعلى هذا لا تسقط نفقتها لأنه بحق.
His statement: '(and if she is preventing herself for the dower)' meaning maintenance is obligatory upon him even if the woman is preventing herself by right, like preventing for receipt of her dower. And what is meant by it is the prompt (dower), either textually or customarily, as we have previously mentioned, because she forfeited ihtibas for a reason from his side, so it is considered as if not forfeited; he made it unrestricted, so it includes prevention after consummation, and this is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: no maintenance for her if she is under the age of puberty due to the invalidity of the father's submission, and we have previously mentioned it. We restricted his statement: 'so a fortiori she is not obliged to spread her goods, etc.' Al-Nahr said: we have previously transmitted from him in the chapter of dower, attributed to al-Mubtagha, that if she is sent to him without a suitable trousseau, he may demand from the father what he paid of dirhams and dinars, unless he remains silent. And upon this, if she is sent to him with it, he is not forbidden from benefiting from it; and in our custom, they commit to a large dower for a large trousseau and a small one for a small trousseau; and there is no doubt that the customary is like the stipulated, so it is appropriate to act according to what has passed. And some virtuous people said: al-Hamawi said after transmitting it: there is consideration in it, because what is in al-Mubtagha is weak, as he himself admitted in the chapter of dower, and custom is only acted upon if it is general; the truth is what is in al-Bahr. His statement: 'and he meant by 'wife' etc.' By the prompt: because if it were all deferred and she refrained, then there is no maintenance for her because it is nushuz, as in Ghayat al-Bayan; and we have previously mentioned that the fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf that she has the right to prevent; accordingly, her maintenance does not fall because it is by right.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding maintenance when a wife prevents herself from submission to receive her prompt dower (mahr mu'ajjal). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that maintenance is due even after consummation if she prevents for the dower, because her prevention is a right (بالحق) and it is analogous to forfeiting ihtibas (detention) for a reason originating from the husband. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they say no maintenance if she is a minor (under puberty) because her father cannot validly submit her. The passage also includes an aside about custom (urf) regarding dowry and trousseau, and then returns to the main issue: if the dower is entirely deferred, her prevention is nushuz (disobedience), so no maintenance. However, the fatwa is on the view of Abu Yusuf that she has the right to prevent, so maintenance remains due. The author relies on the fatwa position, indicating the operative ruling.

Key Terms
مهر معجل (mahr mu'ajjal): The prompt portion of the dower that is due immediately upon the contract.
احتباس (ihtibas): Detention or confinement; the wife's legal right to withhold herself from the husband until receipt of prompt dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No, because it is considered nushuz
C) Only if she is a minor
D) No, because she is not submitting

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that a wife preventing herself for prompt dower is entitled to maintenance because her prevention is by right.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Condition of Maintenance and Definition of Nushuz
Definition of maintenance condition and nushuz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for maintenance (taslim) and define nushuz according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Maintenance is due when the wife submits; nushuz cancels it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the wife's maintenance is conditional upon her submission (taslim). The author then defines nushuz (disobedience) as leaving the husband's house without permission or preventing intimacy without valid excuse. Understanding these concepts is essential for applying the rules of spousal maintenance correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for maintenance
Locate the author's statement that the condition for maintenance is the wife's taslim (submission). Note that this is not unconditional.
The text explicitly says: 'وأشار المصنف إلى أن شرط وجوب النفقة تسليم المرأة'
2
Understand the meaning of taslim
Taslim is defined as takhliyah: the wife vacating herself and removing obstacles to intimacy. This includes both physical presence and not preventing access.
The obstacle can be from her side or from a third party.
3
List scenarios where maintenance is still due despite not living together
The text gives examples: when the husband doesn't demand the move, when she refuses for a valid reason (unpaid dower), or when she asks for a rental house.
These are exceptions to the general rule of living together.
4
Define nushuz from the text
Nushuz is defined linguistically and legally: she who leaves her husband's house without permission or prevents intimacy without right.
The definition is from Imam al-Khassaf and includes both actual leaving and legal obstruction.

Source Text

And the author pointed out that the condition for the obligation of maintenance is the wife's submission of herself to the husband at the time submission is due. And by submission we mean takhliyah, which is that she vacates (herself) between herself and her husband by removing the obstacle to intercourse or enjoyment, if the obstacle is from her side or from other than the husband. So if he marries an adult, free, healthy, sound woman and moves her to his house, she has maintenance; likewise if he does not move her and she is such that she does not prevent herself, and she requests maintenance and he does not demand the move, she has maintenance. If he demands the move and she refuses, then if her refusal is by right, such as refusing to receive her prompt dower, she has maintenance; likewise if he demands the move after he has paid her the dower to a usurped house and she refuses, she has maintenance because it is by right. And if she was living in her house and prevented him from entering upon her, not by way of nushuz, but she said to him: 'Move me to your house or rent a house for me where I may live, for I need this house of mine to take its rent,' she has maintenance; likewise in al-Bada'i. And in al-Dhakhira, and some later scholars from the imams of Balkh said: she does not deserve maintenance if she is not sent to the husband's house; and the fatwa is on the answer of the book, which is maintenance if he does not demand the move. Obligation. His statement: 'not a nashiza' in genitive, coordinated with 'wife,' meaning maintenance is not obligatory for the nashiza, and she is in language the disobedient to the husband, the one who hates him. It is said: the woman nashazat (disobeyed) her husband, so she is nashiza. And from al-Zajjaj: nushuz is between the spouses, and it is the dislike of each one for the other; similarly in al-Mughrab. And in the Shari'ah, as Imam al-Khassaf said: she who leaves her husband's house, preventing herself from him. And by 'leaving' is meant being in other than his house without his permission, to include when she refuses to come to his house initially without payment of her prompt dower, and when she leaves her house after having moved to it; and he released 'leaving' so it includes real and legal, which is her not enabling him to enter her house in which they both reside before she asks for the move, etc. In al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya: and no maintenance in fasid marriage nor in its idda; and if the marriage was valid in appearance, and the judge imposed maintenance on her and she took it for a month, then the invalidity of the marriage appeared, such as the witnesses testifying that she is his foster-sister, and the judge separated them, the husband recovers from the woman what she took. But if he spent without the judge's imposition, he does not recover anything; similarly mentioned by al-Sadr al-Shahid in Sharh Adab al-Qadi, and in al-Dhakhira. And they agreed that in marriage without witnesses, maintenance is due; similarly in al-Khulasa. He said: and it seems that the correct view is that it is not due, for there is no doubt that marriage without witnesses is fasid, and maintenance is only due through ihtibas, and there is no ihtibas in fasid, as we have mentioned at the beginning of this chapter from al-Bada'i. His statement: 'and the author pointed out that the condition for the obligation of maintenance is the submission of the woman, etc.' As for if she does not submit herself to him at the time submission is due, then maintenance is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling explaining the condition for maintenance: the wife's submission (taslim) to her husband. Submission means takhliyah (vacating) by removing any obstacle to intimacy. The author then presents various scenarios: if she is moved to his house, she has maintenance; if she stays in her own house but does not prevent him, she has maintenance; if she refuses to move for a valid reason (like unpaid prompt dower), she has maintenance. If she prevents him from entering her house but not out of nushuz (e.g., she wants him to move her or rent a house), she still has maintenance. The definition of nashiza (disobedient wife) is then given: she who leaves the husband's house without permission or prevents him from intimacy without right. The passage also reiterates that no maintenance is due in a fasid marriage, and discusses a case of apparent valid marriage that turns out invalid: the husband can recover maintenance if it was imposed by a judge, but not if he gave voluntarily. The author also contests a view that marriage without witnesses entitles maintenance, stating clearly that such a marriage is fasid and thus no maintenance.

Key Terms
تسليم (taslim): Submission; the wife's act of being available to her husband without preventing him from lawful intimacy.
نشوز (nushuz): Disobedience of the wife towards her husband by leaving his house without permission or preventing him from intimacy without a valid excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) When she is a minor

Key Takeaway
Maintenance is conditional upon the wife's submission; nushuz negates it.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate

Nushuz and Its Effect on Nafaqah: Hanafi Rulings and Exceptions
Expansion on nushuz and its effect on nafaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when a wife's nushuz cancels her right to maintenance and identify the exceptions that preserve that right.

Core Idea
Nafaqah is dropped by nushuz, but not by every refusal; borrowed maintenance and certain circumstances keep the obligation alive.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the definition of nashizah and the implications for nafaqah. It clarifies that nushuz must involve an unjustified exit or refusal of intimacy, and it introduces a crucial exception: if the wife has borrowed money for maintenance, that debt survives her rebellion. The author also addresses special cases including denial of marriage and the effect of testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two forms of nushuz
Recognize that nushuz consists of either leaving the marital home without legal excuse or unjustifiably preventing the husband from intimacy. The passage states that remaining in the house and refusing intercourse is not considered nushuz because the husband can still obtain his objective.
The key is unjustified action; a valid excuse (e.g., safety, health) prevents nushuz.
2
Determine the effect on nafaqah
Once nushuz is established, the wife loses her right to future maintenance, including any pre-existing obligatory maintenance. The passage says 'nushuz cancels it as well' referring to already obligatory maintenance.
Maintenance already paid is not returned; only future obligation is dropped.
3
Identify the exception for borrowed maintenance
If the wife had previously borrowed money (istidanah) for her maintenance, that debt remains due despite her nushuz. This is based on the sounder narration and is a point worth memorizing.
This exception prevents the husband from exploiting his wife's rebellion to avoid a debt.
4
Recognize non-nushuz situations
The passage lists several scenarios that do not constitute nushuz: leaving a usurped house, refusing to move to a house of doubt (e.g., a sultan's house), and a wife being detained for debt or illness. In these, maintenance continues.
The underlying principle is that nushuz requires the husband's legitimate authority over the residence.
5
Examine procedural issues
If the wife denies the marriage, she has no maintenance while denying, but she regains it if she later confirms. If the husband denies the marriage, maintenance is only suspended during the trial period. Testimony that the wife was not in the husband's house for intimacy is not accepted if it is possible she is being forced.
The burden of proof and the effect of denial are carefully balanced to avoid injustice.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Because she is like one who has left. And excluded is when she left a usurped house or refused to move to it, then she is not a nashizah as we already mentioned, because it is not his house at all, unlike a house with doubt like the sultan's house; she may not refuse and become a nashizah as in al-Khaniyah due to the disregard of doubt in our time as in al-Tajnis. And the constructive exit includes when he asked to travel with her from her town and she refused; then she has no maintenance according to the apparent narration that he has the right to travel with her. And excluded from it is if she hires herself to breastfeed a child and her husband is noble and she does not leave his house; and in al-Fawaid al-Tajiyyah there are two transmissions: the second is as we mentioned, and the first is that it is nushuz even if she does not leave, and its weakness is not hidden. And in al-Khulasa: If the husband says 'She is nashizah, so she has no maintenance from me,' and they testify that he paid her the prompt (mahr) and she was not in the husband's house, the maintenance is dropped. And if they testify that she is not in obedience to the husband for intercourse, it is not accepted because it is probable that she is in his house, and it is necessary to oblige: obliged, and not. His statement: 'Except if she borrowed...' al-Ramli said: 'The discussion is about obligation, not about dropping what... doubt that the nashizah's maintenance is absolutely not obligatory, so the statement of al-Mukhtasar is general, and the statement of this commentator has consideration.'

Nashizah, and a minor who is not had intercourse, and one imprisoned for debt, and one seized, and one in need with other than the husband, and a sick woman who is not in obedience, and she is not in... and by this, maintenance is not dropped because the husband overpowers her.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the role of nushuz (rebellion) in accordance with the Hanafi school. It begins by reaffirming that a wife who leaves the marital home without legal excuse is effectively nashizah (rebellious), even if she remains in the same town. However, if she refuses to move from a usurped house or a house of doubt (like a sultan's residence), she is not nashizah. The author specifies that refusal to engage in intercourse while remaining in the house does not constitute nushuz because the husband can still obtain his objective. A key exception is when a wife has borrowed maintenance money (istidanah): that debt remains her right despite nushuz. The passage also discusses cases where the wife denies the marriage contract: while she denies, she gets no maintenance; if she later affirms, maintenance resumes. If the husband denies the marriage, maintenance is merely suspended during the trial. The author addresses practical scenarios like a wife hiring herself as a wet nurse without leaving the house, noting a weak opinion that this is nushuz. Finally, the issue of testimony: if witnesses say the wife was not in the husband's house at the time of paying prompt dower, maintenance drops; but testimony that she is not obedient for intercourse is insufficient because she might be in his house. The marginal note from al-Ramli clarifies that the discussion is about obligation, not about dropping already accrued maintenance.

Key Terms
ناشزة (nāshizah): A wife who rebels against her husband by leaving the marital home or refusing him without legal right.
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance payable by a husband to his wife, including food, clothing, and shelter.
استدانة (istidānah): The wife borrowing money for her maintenance, often with the husband's implied consent, which remains her right even if she becomes nashizah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When she refuses to cook for her husband
B) When she has borrowed money for maintenance
C) When she leaves the house without permission
D) When she denies the marriage contract

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a balanced approach: nushuz drops future maintenance but preserves pre-existing obligations, and only genuine rebellion is penalized.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Nafaqah for a Minor Wife: The Hanafi Position
Explaining the ruling on maintenance for a minor wife not yet capable of intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafaqah for a minor wife and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and apply the principle of tamkin to determine nafaqah obligation.

Core Idea
A minor wife receives mahr, not nafaqah, because nafaqah requires the possibility of sexual enjoyment.

The marriage contract creates rights and duties, but not all are immediate. One key duty is nafaqah (maintenance), which the Hanafis tie to the wife's ability to provide tamkin (submission for intercourse). This lesson examines the ruling for a minor wife who cannot yet be consummated, a scenario that triggers a famous disagreement with the Shafi'i school. We will dissect the evidence and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on nafaqah for a minor wife (ṣaghīrah) who cannot bear intercourse. Identify the hukm: it is not wajib (obligatory). Note the basis: the prevention of enjoyment is due to a characteristic in her (the minor).
Contrast with a sick wife (marīḍah) who does receive nafaqah because her condition is temporary and she can still be present.
2
Locate the dalil for the Hanafi position
The text gives the Hanafi dalil: nafaqah is a compensation for tamkin (submission for enjoyment). Since the minor cannot provide tamkin, no nafaqah is due. Additionally, mahr is the compensation for ownership (milk), and two compensations for one exchange cannot be combined.
The Shafi'i dalil is also given: nafaqah is a return for ownership by marriage, analogous to a slave-girl. The Hanafi response clarifies the distinction.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the Hanafi dalil prove the ruling? The legal cause (ʿillah) for nafaqah is tamkin (actual or potential). The minor lacks this, so the ʿillah is absent, and the ruling (wujūb) does not apply. Mahr, on the other hand, is due at contract and is the sole compensation for ownership.
This is a qiyās jalī (clear analogy) based on the concept of compensation for benefits.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that nafaqah is due because it is a return for ownership (milk), not specifically for tamkin. For him, the bond of marriage alone creates the obligation, like owning a slave-girl.
The Hanafi response: that duplicates compensation (mahr for ownership, nafaqah for same). The mahr is the exclusive price of ownership, so nafaqah cannot also be for ownership.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical difference: A Shafi'i husband must pay nafaqah to a minor wife; a Hanafi husband does not. The text follows the Hanafi position as the relied-upon (muftā bihī).
This ruling applies regardless of where the wife lives (husband's house or father's house) and regardless of the husband's age (even if minor).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصغيرة لا توطأ) أي لا نفقة للصغيرة إذا كانت لا تطيق الجماع لأن امتناع الاستمتاع لمعنى فيها والاحتباس الموجب هو الذي يكون وسيلة إلى المقصود المستحق بالنكاح ولم يوجد بخلاف المريضة كما سيأتي . وقال الشافعي لها النفقة لأنها عوض عن الملك عنده كما في المملوكة بملك اليمين ولنا أن المهر عوض عن الملك ولا يجتمع العوضان عن معوض واحد فلها المهر دون النفقة أطلق في عدم وجوبها لها فشمل ما إذا كانت في بيت الزوج أو في بيت أبيها، وقيد بالنفقة لأن للأب مطالبة الزوج بمهر الصغيرة التي لا توطأ وإن كانت صغيرة جداً ويجبر الزوج على دفع المهر إليه لأنه يجب كله بنفس العقد وحق القبض للأب؛ كذا في الخانية. وقيد بالصغيرة لأنها تجب كالمهر للكبيرة وإن كان الزوج صغيراً جداً في ماله لأن العجز من قبله كالمجبوب والعنيين فإن لم يكن له مال لا تجب على الأب نفقة امرأة ولده ويستدين الأب عليه ثم يرجع بذلك على الابن إذا أيسر؛ كذا في الخانية. وفي الخلاصة : لا يجب على أبيه إلا إذا ضمنها كما في المهر ا هـ . فلو أنفق عليها أبوه ثم ولدت واعترفت أنها حبلت من الزنا فإنها لا ترد شيئاً من النفقة لأن الحبل من الزنا، وإن منع من الوطء لا يمنع من دواعيه ومن الوطء فيما دون الفرج وهذا كاف لوجوب النفقة بخلاف ما إذا أقرت أنها حين تزوجت كانت حبلى فإنها ترد نفقة ستة أشهر لأنه لا نفقة في النكاح الفاسد حملاً لأمرها على أن الحبل من زوج آخر سابق فتصدق في حق نفسها لا في حق الزوج؛ كذا في الذخيرة. والحاصل أن الصغيرة التي لا توطأ لا يجب لها نفقة صغيراً أو كبيراً، والمطيقة للوطء تجب نفقتها صغيراً كان الزوج أو كبيراً، واختلف في كان الزوج ظاهر تأمل قوله : قلت وبهذا عرف جواب واقعة الخ) هو من كلام المجتبى . قال في النهر : وفيه نظر سيأتي إيضاحه . قوله : (مع أنه سيأتي أن القابلة لها الخروج قال الرملي : قيده في الخانية بإذن الزوج وأما بدون البحر الرائق / ج ٤ / م ٢٠ -
His statement: (And a minor who is not had intercourse) i.e., there is no maintenance for the minor if she cannot bear intercourse, because the prevention of enjoyment is due to a characteristic in her, and the required confinement (of the wife) is that which is a means to the purpose owed by marriage, and it does not exist, unlike the sick woman as will come. And al-Shafi'i said: She has maintenance because it is a compensation for ownership according to him, like in the slave-girl by right hand possession. And we (Hanafis) (argue): The mahr is compensation for ownership, and two compensations cannot be combined for one exchange, so she has the mahr without maintenance. He made absolute the non-obligation of it for her, so it includes whether she is in the husband's house or in her father's house. And he restricted by maintenance because the father has the right to claim the mahr of the minor who is not had intercourse, even if she is very young, and the husband is compelled to pay the mahr to him because it becomes entirely obligatory by the contract itself, and the right of receipt belongs to the father; thus in al-Khaniyah. And he restricted by 'minor' because it (maintenance) becomes obligatory like the mahr for an adult (wife) even if the husband is very young in his wealth, because the incapacity is from his side, like the impotent and the castrated. If he has no wealth, the father is not obliged to provide maintenance for his son's wife, but the father borrows on his behalf and then recovers from the son when he becomes wealthy; thus in al-Khaniyah. And in al-Khulasa: It is not obligatory on his father unless he guarantees it, like in the mahr. So if his father spent on her, then she gave birth and admitted that she became pregnant from fornication, she does not return anything of the maintenance because the pregnancy is from fornication; and although it prevents intercourse, it does not prevent its desires and intercourse below the private parts, and this is sufficient for the obligation of maintenance. Unlike if she admitted that at the time of marriage she was pregnant, then she returns maintenance of six months because there is no maintenance in an invalid marriage, construing her matter that the pregnancy is from a previous other husband; so she is believed regarding herself, not regarding the husband; thus in al-Dhakhirah. The summary is that the minor who cannot be had intercourse: no maintenance is obligatory for her whether the husband is minor or adult, and the (wife) who is capable of intercourse: her maintenance is obligatory whether the husband is minor or adult. And there is difference regarding if the husband is (minor?) apparent contemplation. His statement: 'I said: And by this the answer to an incident of our time is known...' is from the speech of al-Mujtaba. He said in al-Nahr: 'And there is consideration in it, its clarification will come.' His statement: 'Although it will come that the midwife has the right to exit' – al-Ramli said: 'He restricted it in al-Khaniyah with the permission of the husband; but without... al-Bahr al-Raiq / vol.4 / p.20 -'
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage addresses the nafaqah of a minor wife who is too young for sexual intercourse. The Hanafi position is that she is not entitled to maintenance because the legal basis of nafaqah is the wife's availability for enjoyment (tamkin). Since she cannot fulfill this, there is no obligation. This is a rule, not a punishment. The text contrasts this with a sick wife who does receive maintenance because her illness is temporary and she can still be present. The Shafi'i position is presented: they argue that nafaqah is a return for ownership (milk) by marriage, analogous to a slave-girl. The Hanafi rebuttal is that mahr is the compensation for ownership, and there cannot be two compensations for one thing (i.e., mahr and nafaqah). Therefore, she has mahr but not nafaqah. The passage then discusses details: if the minor lives with her father or husband, the ruling is the same. The father can claim the mahr because it becomes due at contract. If the husband is a minor, the father of the husband is not liable for his wife's nafaqah unless he guarantees it; instead he may borrow and later recover from his son. A pregnant woman's maintenance is still due even if she became pregnant from zina, because intercourse below the private parts is still possible and fulfills the purpose. But if she admits pregnancy before marriage (implying invalid marriage), she must return six months of nafaqah. The summary reiterates that a minor incapable of intercourse gets no nafaqah, while a capable wife does, regardless of the husband's age. The text ends with a reference to a contemporary incident about female workers (in factories) and notes that a midwife may exit with the husband's permission.

Key Terms
صغيرة (ṣaghīrah): A female minor who has not reached puberty and is not yet capable of sexual intercourse.
تمكين (tamkīn): The wife's submission and availability for sexual relations, which is the basis for the husband's obligation of nafaqah.
مهر (mahr): The dower paid to the wife at marriage, which the Hanafis consider the exclusive compensation for the ownership of marital benefits.
عوض (ʿiwaḍ): Compensation or consideration in a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on nafaqah for a minor wife who cannot be sexually enjoyed?
A) She is entitled to nafaqah because the marriage contract creates an obligation
B) She is not entitled to nafaqah because she cannot provide tamkin (submission for intercourse)
C) She is entitled to nafaqah only if she lives in her husband's house
D) She is entitled to nafaqah only if she is at least nine years old

Key Takeaway
A minor wife who cannot be consummated is not entitled to nafaqah in the Hanafi school because nafaqah is tied to the ability to provide sexual enjoyment (tamkin), not merely to ownership.
