Nafaqah — Maintenance
beginner
6 min
No Maintenance for Wife Imprisoned, Abducted, or Sick Before Handover
Ruling on maintenance for absent wives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance for wives whose absence is not attributable to the husband, and apply the condition of ihtibas (confinement) to these cases.

Core Idea
The wife's confinement in the husband's home is the basis for maintenance; if her absence is not his doing, maintenance falls.

In Hanafi fiqh, a wife's right to maintenance (nafaqah) is tied to her being in the husband's home (ihtibas). But what if she is absent due to imprisonment, abduction, or illness before transfer? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that in such cases maintenance is not obligatory because the loss of confinement is not attributable to the husband. We will examine these rulings and the underlying analogy to a rented object seized from a lessee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four cases
List the wives mentioned: imprisoned for debt, abducted, occupied with a need for someone other than husband, sick not yet handed over.
These are forms of absence not caused by the husband.
2
State the ruling
For all four, maintenance is not obligatory. The text states: 'لا تجب النفقة لهؤلاء'.
The ruling is clear and unconditional.
3
Explain the rationale
The reason is 'لأن فوات الاحتباس ليس منه' – the loss of confinement is not from the husband. The condition of ihtibas is not met.
Even if the wife is not at fault, the husband is not responsible.
4
Analyze the imprisoned case
The text specifies that the loss of confinement is attributed to the wife's procrastination (مماطلة) in paying debt. Even if she is unable, it is still not from the husband.
This covers both able and unable women, before or after transfer to husband's home.
5
Note the qiyas
Imam Muhammad cited an analogy: if a rented item is seized from the lessee, the rent falls because the loss of benefit is not from the lessor. Similarly, maintenance falls here.
This strengthens the ruling by analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومحبوسة بدين ومغصوبة وحاجة مع غير الزوج ومريضة لم تزف) أي لا تجب النفقة لهؤلاء لأن فوات الاحتباس ليس منه، أما في المحبوسة بدين فلان فوات الاحتباس منها بالمماطلة وإن لم يكن منها بأن كانت عاجزة فليس منه ولذا أطلقه المصنف ليشمل ما إذا كانت قادرة على ادائه أولاً، وما إذا حبست قبل النقلة وبعدها هو المذكور في الجامع الكبير . واستشهد له محمد رحمه الله بغصب العين المستأجرة من يد المستأجر حيث تسقط الأجرة عنه لفوات الانتفاع لا من جهته وعليه الاعتماد ؛ كذا في التبيين وفي فتح القدير وعليه الفتوى،
His statement: (And a woman imprisoned for debt, abducted, or occupied with a need with someone other than the husband, and a sick woman who has not been handed over) i.e., maintenance is not obligatory for these, because the loss of confinement is not from him. As for the imprisoned for debt, the loss of confinement is from her through procrastination, even if it is not from her in the sense that she is unable, it is not from him. Thus the author made it absolute to include whether she is able to pay or not, and whether she was imprisoned before relocation or after, as mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) cited as evidence the seizure of a rented object from the lessee's hand, where the rent falls due to loss of benefit not from his side, and reliance is upon this. As in al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir; and the fatwa is upon it.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for four categories of wives who are not receiving nafaqah: (1) a wife imprisoned for debt, (2) a wife abducted, (3) a wife occupied with a need for someone other than her husband, and (4) a sick wife who has not yet been transferred to the husband's home. In all these cases, the absence of the wife from the husband's home is not due to any action on his part. Hence, the confinement (ihtibas) that would normally obligate maintenance is not present. The commentator clarifies that even if the imprisoned wife is unable to pay the debt, the loss of confinement is still attributed to her because the debt is her responsibility. An analogy is drawn to a rented object that is seized from the lessee: rent falls due to loss of benefit not from the lessor. The fatwa is upon this ruling.

Key Terms
محبوسة بدين (maḥbūsah bi-dayn): A wife imprisoned due to a debt she owes, causing her absence from the marital home.
فوات الاحتباس (fawāt al-iḥtibās): The failure of the wife's confinement in the husband's home, which is a condition for maintenance.
مغصوبة (maghṣūbah): A wife taken away by force (abducted).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a wife who is imprisoned for debt is not entitled to maintenance because:
A) The husband is not responsible for her debts.
B) The loss of her presence is attributed to her.
C) She can be divorced easily.
D) Imprisonment nullifies the marriage.

Key Takeaway
Maintenance is not due if the wife's absence from the home is not caused by the husband.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
8 min
Nafaqah Drops When Confinement is Lost from the Wife's Side
Ruling with proof via qiyas and intra-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafaqah for a wife imprisoned for debt or kidnapped, and explain the legal basis using the principle of fawat al-ihtibas and the qiyas on leased property.

Core Idea
Nafaqah drops when the wife is not confined for the husband, even if the cause is involuntary.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains when a wife loses her right to nafaqah despite being married. The key principle is that nafaqah is compensation for the wife's confinement (ihtibas) for the husband's benefit. If that confinement is lost due to a cause not attributable to the husband, nafaqah drops—even if the wife is not at fault. We will analyze two cases: a woman imprisoned for debt and a kidnapped woman, along with the qiyas that supports the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for each case
The passage states that a woman imprisoned for debt (mahbusa biddayn) and a woman kidnapped (maghsubah) are not entitled to nafaqah. Note the nuance: for the kidnapped woman, Abu Yusuf disagreed, but the fatwa is on the majority view.
The ruling is the same for both despite different causes.
2
Understand the underlying principle: fawat al-ihtibas
Nafaqah is tied to the wife being confined for the husband. If confinement is lost, nafaqah drops. The key is whether the loss is attributable to the husband or not. If from the wife or a third party not acting for the husband, nafaqah drops.
The principle is also applied when the husband is imprisoned (wife retains nafaqah because loss is from his side).
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy) presented by Muhammad al-Shaybani
Imam Muhammad draws an analogy with a leased item usurped from the lessee: just as rent drops because the benefit is lost not from the lessor's side, so nafaqah drops when confinement is lost not from the husband's side. Identify the asl (leased item), hukm (rent drops), illa (benefit lost not from owner/lessor), and far' (wife imprisoned).
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) because the illa is extracted from the principle of benefit being lost from the party responsible.
4
Evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute on the kidnapped woman
Abu Yusuf held that a kidnapped woman still gets nafaqah because the loss of confinement is not from her (she is coerced). The majority responded that even though it is not from her, it is also not from the husband, so confinement cannot be presumed to continue. The fatwa follows the majority.
This dispute highlights the strictness of the condition: confinement must actually be for the husband's benefit.
5
Apply the rule to other scenarios
The text also notes that if the husband is imprisoned (even unjustly), the wife retains nafaqah because the loss is from his side. This shows the rule is symmetrical: only acts attributable to the wife or third parties break the obligation.
The cause matters more than fault: even wrongful imprisonment of husband is from his side.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومحبوسة بدين ومغصوبة وحاجة مع غير الزوج ومريضة لم تزف) أي لا تجب النفقة لهؤلاء لأن فوات الاحتباس ليس منه، أما في المحبوسة بدين فلان فوات الاحتباس منها بالمماطلة وإن لم يكن منها بأن كانت عاجزة فليس منه ولذا أطلقه المصنف ليشمل ما إذا كانت قادرة على ادائه أولاً، وما إذا حبست قبل النقلة وبعدها هو المذكور في الجامع الكبير . واستشهد له محمد رحمه الله بغصب العين المستأجرة من يد المستأجر حيث تسقط الأجرة عنه لفوات الانتفاع لا من جهته وعليه الاعتماد ؛ كذا في التبيين وفي فتح القدير وعليه الفتوى، لا وفي غاية البيان أن محمداً وضع المسألة في النفقة المفروضة لأنه بدونه لا تتصور المسألة لسقوطها، ولو حذف المصنف قوله بدين لكان أولى لأن المحبوسة ظلماً بغير حق لا نفقة لها لأن المعتبر في سقوط نفقتها فوات الاحتباس لا من جهة الزوج وقد فات الاحتباس هنا من جهته، وهذا هو الصحيح لأنه إذا كان الفوات من جهته أمكن القول ببقائه تقديراً، وأما إذا كان لا من جهته فلم يكن الاحتباس باقياً تقديراً وبدونه لا يمكن إيجاب النفقة؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وقيد بحبسها لأن الزوج لو حبس وهو يقدر على الأداء أو لا يقدر أو حبس ظلماً أو هرب أو نشز كانت لها النفقة لأن الاحتباس هنا فات لمعنى من جهة الزوج ؛ كذا في الذخيرة ولا فرق بين أن تحبسه هي لدين لها عليه أو يحبسه أجنبي. وفي الخلاصة أنها إذا حبسته وطلب أن تحبس معه فإنها لا تحبس. وذكر في مآل الفتاوى أنه إذا خيف عليها الفساد معه عند المتأخرين، وأما إذا غصبها رجل كرهاً وذهب بها فما في المختصر هو . الرواية، وعن أبي يوسف أن لها النفقة والفتوى على الأول لأن فوت الاحتباس ليس منه ليجعل باقياً تقديراً؛ كذا في الهداية.
His saying: (And a woman imprisoned for debt, and a kidnapped [woman], and a [woman] performing Hajj with someone other than the husband, and a sick woman who has not been handed over) - i.e., maintenance is not obligatory for these, because the loss of confinement is not from him. As for the woman imprisoned for debt, the loss of confinement is from her due to procrastination, even if it is not from her if she is incapable, so it is not from him. Therefore, the author made it absolute to include whether she is able to pay off the debt or not, and whether she was imprisoned before the transfer [to the husband's house] or after; that is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) cited as evidence the case of a leased item being usurped from the lessee's hand, where the rent drops from him due to the loss of benefit, not from his side, and upon it is reliance; thus in al-Tabyeen and in Fath al-Qadir, and upon it the fatwa. No, and in Ghayat al-Bayan that Muhammad placed the case in the context of obligatory maintenance, because without it the case cannot be imagined due to its dropping. And if the author had omitted his word 'for debt', it would have been better, because the woman imprisoned wrongfully without right has no maintenance, for the consideration in dropping her maintenance is the loss of confinement, not from the husband's side; and here the confinement has been lost from his side. This is the correct view, because if the loss is from his side, one could say that [confinement] remains in consideration, but if it is not from his side, then confinement does not remain in consideration, and without it maintenance cannot be imposed; thus in al-Dhakhirah. And he restricted it by her imprisonment, because if the husband is imprisoned, whether he is able to pay or not, or is imprisoned wrongfully, or flees, or is defiant, she has maintenance, because the confinement here is lost due to a meaning from the husband's side; thus in al-Dhakhirah. And there is no difference between whether she imprisons him for a debt he owes her or if an outsider imprisons him. In al-Khulasa, if she imprisons him and asks to be imprisoned with him, she is not imprisoned. And it is mentioned in Ma'al al-Fatawa that if there is fear of corruption with him according to the later scholars. And as for if a man kidnaps her forcibly and takes her away, then what is in al-Mukhtar is the [established] narration, and from Abu Yusuf that she has maintenance, and the fatwa is upon the first, because the loss of confinement is not from him so that it can be considered remaining in consideration; thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage explains categories of women who are not entitled to nafaqah according to the Hanafi school. The key principle is that nafaqah is compensation for the wife's confinement (ihtibas) for the husband's benefit. If that confinement is lost due to the wife's own action or a cause not attributable to the husband, nafaqah drops. The first case is a woman imprisoned for debt (mahbusa biddayn). Even if she cannot pay (i.e., incapable), the loss of confinement is still considered from her side because she incurred the debt, so no nafaqah. A similar analogy is given: if a leased item is usurped from the lessee, the rent drops because the benefit is lost, not from the lessor's side. The correct view is that if the husband is imprisoned, wife still gets nafaqah because the loss is from his side. Similarly, if a woman is kidnapped against her will, the established narration (zahir al-riwaya) says she gets no nafaqah, though Abu Yusuf said she does. The fatwa is on the first view because the confinement is not from the husband's side and cannot be presumed to continue.

Key Terms
محبوسة بدين (mahbusa biddayn): A woman imprisoned because she owes a debt; she loses nafaqah as the confinement is considered lost due to her own cause.
مغصوبة (maghsubah): A woman kidnapped against her will; no nafaqah in the fatwa position.
فوات الاحتباس (fawat al-ihtibas): The loss of the wife's confinement for the husband; if it happens from her side, nafaqah drops.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi position, does a husband owe nafaqah to his wife if she is kidnapped by a stranger?
A) Yes, because she is not at fault.
B) Yes, because the marriage contract continues.
C) No, because the confinement is lost from neither side, so cannot be considered remaining.
D) No, because the wife is considered nashiz.

Key Takeaway
Nafaqah is compensation for confinement; if confinement is lost from any cause not attributable to the husband, he is not obligated to pay.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate

Nafaqah During Wife's Hajj and for Sick Wife Before Transfer
Rulings with proof: exceptions to nafaqah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a wife's nafaqah drops due to her absence (Hajj) or illness before transfer, and identify the Hanafi position including the intra-madhhab difference.

Core Idea
Nafaqah drops when the wife's own action or condition prevents confinement, even for obligatory acts.

We have seen that nafaqah is generally wajib upon the husband for his wife as long as she is available (tamkin). In this passage, Shaykh Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym explains two exceptions: when the wife travels for Hajj without her husband, and when she is sick and still in her own home before the marriage is consummated. The underlying principle is that the loss of confinement (fawat al-ihtibas) originates from her side, so the obligation falls. An intra-madhhab difference from Abu Yusuf is noted, but the fatwa follows the majority view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exceptions to nafaqah
Read the passage and list the two scenarios where nafaqah is not obligatory: (1) wife performs Hajj with someone other than her husband, (2) sick woman who has not been moved to the husband's house.
Both involve the wife not being in the husband's confinement due to her own cause.
2
Extract the general principle
The passage states 'because the loss of confinement is from her'. This is the ratio legis: any absence caused by the wife's choice or condition (even a valid excuse like obligatory Hajj) drops nafaqah.
Contrast with fasting and prayer: these do not prevent confinement, so nafaqah remains.
3
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on Hajj
Abu Yusuf holds that for Hajj al-Islam (obligatory), the wife retains maintenance of residence (nafaqah al-hadar) because performing a fard is an excuse. The fatwa, however, is on the first view (no nafaqah).
Al-Dhakhirah records a narration that the husband should accompany her and spend then.
4
Differentiate the sick woman ruling
If the wife falls sick before moving to the husband's house, she is not in his confinement, so no nafaqah. If she falls sick after being in his house, nafaqah continues because confinement was established.
The healthy wife who does not prevent transfer gets nafaqah even if not demanded.
5
Recognize the court remedy for arrears
The passage ends with a separate rule: if the husband delays maintenance, the wife can seek a court order; arrears become a debt and the husband may be imprisoned.
This is not directly about the exceptions but shows how nafaqah is enforced.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا حجت مع غير الزوج فلأن فوات الاحتباس منها . . وعن أبي يوسف أن لها النفقة لأن إقامة الفرض عذر فيكون لها نفقة الحضر. وفي رواية عنه يؤمر الزوج بالخروج معها والإنفاق عليها إذا أرادت حجة الإسلام؛ الذخيرة. أطلق الحج فشمل الفرض والنفل وما إذا حجت قبل أن تسلم نفسها أو بعده وهذا . ظاهر الرواية لأن الامتناع من جهتها فأوجب سقوطها، سواء كانت عاصية في الخروج أو طائعة بخلاف الصلاة والصوم لوجود الاحتباس فلا يمنع اشتغالها بهما من وجوب النفقة؛ كذا في الذخيرة . وقيد بكون الحج مع غير الزوج الشامل لحجها وحدها أو مع محرم للاحتراز عما إذا حج معها فإن لها النفقة اتفاقاً وهي نفقة الحضر لا السفر فينظر إلى قيمة الطعام في الحضر ولا ينظر إلى قيمته في السفر، ولا يلزمه الكراء ومؤنة السفر، وأما المريضة التي لم تزف فالمراد بها المريضة التي لم تنتقل إلى بيت الزوج، وقد اختلفت عبارات الكتب في هذه المسألة فظاهر المختصر أنها إذا مرضت قبل الدخول وهي في غير بيت الزوج فإنه لا نفقة لها، ومفهومه أنها إن كانت في بيته فلها النفقة. وعلى هذا فالفرق بينها وبين الصحيحة إنما هو من جهة أن الصحيحة إذا لم تمنع نفسها من الانتقال مع الزوج فلها النفقة طلبها الزوج أو لا بخلاف المريضة فإنه لا نفقة لها وهي في بيتها مطلقاً. وفي البدائع ما يخالفه فإنه قال : لو مع الصداق قوله : (وذكر في مآل الفتاوى أنه إذا خيف الخ) وفي التتارخانية : فإن ماطلها بالنفقة وسألت القاضي أن يفرض لها نفقة فعل ذلك ويكون ما اجتمع عليه من النفقة بعد الفرض ديناً . فيستديم الحبس إلى أن يوفي الكل. فإن قال الزوج للقاضي أحبسها معي فإن لي موضعاً في الحبس
And as for if she performs Hajj with someone other than the husband, then because the loss of confinement is from her. And from Abu Yusuf that she has maintenance, because performing the obligation is an excuse, so she has maintenance of residence. And in a narration from him, the husband is ordered to go out with her and spend on her if she wants to perform Hajj al-Islam; al-Dhakhirah. He made absolute the Hajj, so it includes obligatory and supererogatory, and whether she performs it before or after surrendering herself. This is the apparent narration because the refusal is from her side, so it necessitated its dropping, whether she is disobedient in going out or obedient, unlike prayer and fasting, because confinement exists, so her engagement in them does not prevent the obligation of maintenance; thus in al-Dhakhirah. And he restricted by the Hajj being with other than the husband, which includes her going alone or with a mahram, to exclude the case where he performs Hajj with her, for then she has maintenance by agreement, and it is maintenance of residence, not travel, so the value of food in the residence is considered, not its value during travel; and he is not liable for hire and travel expenses. And as for the sick woman who has not been handed over, what is meant is the sick woman who has not transferred to the husband's house. The statements of the books have differed on this issue. The apparent of al-Mukhtar is that if she falls sick before consummation and she is in a house other than the husband's, then there is no maintenance for her; its implication is that if she is in his house, she has maintenance. On this basis, the difference between her and the healthy woman is that the healthy woman, if she does not prevent herself from moving with the husband, has maintenance whether the husband asks for it or not, unlike the sick woman, for she has no maintenance while in her home absolutely. And in al-Bada'i' what contradicts it, for he said: The end of the sentence: '...with the dower'. His saying: 'And it is mentioned in Ma'al al-Fatawa that if he fears corruption, etc.' And in al-Tatarkhaniyyah: if he procrastinates on the maintenance and she asks the judge to impose maintenance for her, he does that, and what accumulates of maintenance after the imposition becomes a debt. He continues the imprisonment until he pays all. If the husband says to the judge: 'Imprison her with me, for I have a place in the prison.'
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage covers two additional cases where nafaqah is not obligatory: when the wife performs Hajj (whether obligatory or supererogatory) with someone other than her husband, and when the wife is sick and has not yet moved to the husband's house (i.e., before consummation). The principle remains that if the absence from confinement is due to the wife's own action, nafaqah drops. For Hajj, even if it is an act of worship, the wife's absence is her choice, so no nafaqah. Abu Yusuf differed, saying that for obligatory Hajj, the wife is excused and should still get maintenance of residence (not travel expenses), but the fatwa is on the first view. For the sick woman, if she is still in her own home and prevents the husband from taking her by reason of sickness, she gets no nafaqah. However, if she was already in his house when she fell ill, she does get nafaqah because the confinement was already established. The text then digresses into a separate ruling about the husband's procrastination of maintenance: if he delays, the wife can seek a court order, and the accumulated arrears become a debt, and the husband may be imprisoned until he pays. If the husband asks for his wife to be imprisoned with him (for her own protection), it may be allowed if there is fear of corruption.

Key Terms
حاجة مع غير الزوج (hajjah ma'a ghayr al-zawj): A wife performing Hajj without her husband; she loses nafaqah during the journey.
مريضة لم تزف (maridah lam tuzaf): A sick woman who has not been transferred to the husband's house; no nafaqah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on nafaqah for a wife who performs Hajj with her husband?
A) No nafaqah because confinement is broken.
B) She receives nafaqah of residence (hadar) by agreement.
C) She receives full travel expenses including hire.
D) The husband must pay costs only if the Hajj is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Nafaqah drops when the wife's own action or condition removes her from the husband's confinement, even for valid reasons like obligatory worship or sickness, unless the husband accompanies her.

Imprisonment and Maintenance: The Principle of Ihtibas
Ruling on wife's nafaqah when husband is imprisoned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife's maintenance when her husband is imprisoned and apply the principle of ihtibas (custody) to determine when maintenance is wajib.

Core Idea
Maintenance is tied to custody; if custody is lost due to the husband, it is considered remaining, so maintenance continues.

This passage from Bahar al-Raiq clarifies a common question: does a wife lose her right to maintenance if her husband is imprisoned? The answer depends on who caused the loss of marital custody (ihtibas). The Hanafi school uses the concept of taqdir (consideration) to preserve obligations even when physical custody is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
Determine the act (wife's maintenance) and its legal classification (wajib) when the husband is imprisoned.
Maintenance is wajib, not fard, because it is established by zanni dalil.
2
Locate the Legal Principle
Recognize that maintenance is based on the husband's right of ihtibas (custody). The passage states that if custody is lost, maintenance falls, but the key question is who caused the loss.
Ihtibas is the husband's right to keep his wife in his home.
3
Determine the Cause of Loss of Custody
If the loss is from the husband's side (e.g., he is imprisoned, flees, or is nashiz), custody is considered remaining (taqdiran) and maintenance continues. If the loss is not from the husband (e.g., wife imprisoned by a stranger), custody is truly lost and maintenance ceases.
This is the core distinction in the passage.
4
Apply to Specific Cases
Apply the principle to various scenarios: husband imprisoned (maintenance yes), wife imprisoned by stranger (maintenance no according to the riwaya), wife performing hajj without husband (maintenance no because loss from her side).
Abu Yusuf differs in the latter two cases, but the fatwa is on the first view.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that a wife imprisoned unjustly or performing obligatory hajj gets maintenance. The majority of later scholars follow the zahir al-riwayah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي غاية البيان أن محمداً وضع المسألة في النفقة المفروضة لأنه بدونه لا تتصور المسألة لسقوطها، ولو حذف المصنف قوله بدين لكان أولى لأن المحبوسة ظلماً بغير حق لا نفقة لها لأن المعتبر في سقوط نفقتها فوات الاحتباس لا من جهة الزوج وقد فات الاحتباس هنا من جهته، وهذا هو الصحيح لأنه إذا كان الفوات من جهته أمكن القول ببقائه تقديراً، وأما إذا كان لا من جهته فلم يكن الاحتباس باقياً تقديراً وبدونه لا يمكن إيجاب النفقة؛ كذا في الذخيرة. وقيد بحبسها لأن الزوج لو حبس وهو يقدر على الأداء أو لا يقدر أو حبس ظلماً أو هرب أو نشز كانت لها النفقة لأن الاحتباس هنا فات لمعنى من جهة الزوج  كذا في الذخيرة ولا فرق بين أن تحبسه هي لدين لها عليه أو يحبسه أجنبي. وفي الخلاصة أنها إذا حبسته وطلب أن تحبس معه فإنها لا تحبس. وذكر في مآل الفتاوى أنه إذا خيف عليها الفساد معه عند المتأخرين، وأما إذا غصبها رجل كرهاً وذهب بها فما في المختصر هو الرواية، وعن أبي يوسف أن لها النفقة والفتوى على الأول لأن فوت الاحتباس ليس منه ليجعل باقياً تقديراً؛ كذا في الهداية. وأما إذا حجت مع غير الزوج فلأن فوات الاحتباس منها . . وعن أبي يوسف أن لها النفقة لأن إقامة الفرض عذر فيكون لها نفقة الحضر. وفي رواية عنه يؤمر الزوج بالخروج معها والإنفاق عليها إذا أرادت حجة الإسلام؛ الذخيرة. أطلق الحج فشمل الفرض والنفل وما إذا حجت قبل أن تسلم نفسها أو بعده وهذا ظاهر الرواية لأن الامتناع من جهتها فأوجب سقوطها، سواء كانت عاصية في الخروج أو طائعة بخلاف الصلاة والصوم لوجود الاحتباس فلا يمنع اشتغالها بهما من وجوب النفقة؛
And in Ghayat al-Bayan: Muhammad placed the issue on the obligatory maintenance because without it the issue cannot be conceived due to its lapse. If the author had omitted his statement 'by debt' it would have been better, because the woman imprisoned unjustly without right has no maintenance, since the consideration in the lapse of her maintenance is the loss of custody (ihtibas) not from the husband's side, and custody here was lost from his side. And this is correct, because if the loss is from his side, it is possible to say it remains consideratively; but if not from his side, then custody does not remain consideratively, and without it maintenance cannot be wajib. Thus in al-Dhakhira. And he qualified it with her imprisonment, because if the husband is imprisoned — whether he is able to pay or not, or imprisoned unjustly, or fled, or was nashiz — then she has maintenance, because here custody was lost due to a meaning from the husband's side. Thus in al-Dhakhira. There is no difference between her imprisoning him for a debt due to her or an outsider imprisoning him. And in al-Khulasa: if she imprisons him and he asks that she be imprisoned with him, she is not imprisoned. And it is mentioned in Ma'al al-Fatawa that if harm to her is feared with him according to the later scholars. And if a man abducts her forcibly and takes her away, what is in al-Mukhtar is the riwaya; and from Abu Yusuf that she has maintenance, and the fatwa is on the first, because the loss of custody is not from him to be considered remaining. Thus in al-Hidaya.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage from Bahar al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the effect of imprisonment on the wife's maintenance (nafaqah). It begins by clarifying that Imam Muhammad framed the issue assuming the maintenance is already wajib (obligatory), because if it were not, the discussion would be moot. The core principle is that maintenance is tied to the husband's custody (ihtibas) over the wife. If the custody is lost, maintenance falls. The key question: who caused the loss? If the loss is due to the husband (such as his own imprisonment for debt or oppression), then custody is considered to remain legally (taqdiran), so maintenance continues. But if the loss is not from the husband (e.g., wife imprisoned unjustly by a third party who is not the husband), then custody is truly lost, and she has no maintenance, because the husband cannot be deemed to have custody over her in prison. The passage then notes: if the husband is imprisoned (any cause), she has maintenance because the loss is from his side. If she herself imprisons him for a debt, she is not imprisoned alongside him. Later scholars said if harm is feared for her, she may not be imprisoned. The fatwa is on the first view: if she is taken forcibly by a stranger, she has no maintenance according to the riwaya, though Abu Yusuf held she does. Then the passage transitions to pilgrimage: if she performs hajj with someone other than her husband, custody is lost from her side, so no maintenance. Abu Yusuf again differed, saying the obligatory hajj is an excuse so she gets maintenance. The passage concludes with a contrast: prayer and fasting do not negate maintenance because custody remains.

Key Terms
الاحتباس (al-ihtibas): The legal custody or right of the husband to keep his wife in his home, upon which maintenance is based.
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance, consisting of food, clothing, and shelter, wajib upon the husband for the wife.
تقديراً (taqdiran): Consideratively; i.e., the law deems custody to exist even if physically absent, to preserve the obligation of maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if the husband is imprisoned unjustly, does the wife still receive maintenance?
A) Yes, because the loss of custody is from the husband's side, so it is considered remaining.
B) No, because imprisonment abolishes custody entirely.
C) Yes, but only if she demands it from the judge.
D) No, because she must live with her family.

Key Takeaway
The wife's maintenance in Hanafi fiqh depends on the cause of loss of custody; if the husband causes it, maintenance continues; if not, it falls.

Wife's Hajj Without Husband: Effect on Maintenance
Ruling on wife's maintenance when she performs hajj without husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife's maintenance when she travels for hajj without her husband, and distinguish the Zahir al-Riwayah position from the view of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A wife loses maintenance if she travels for hajj because custody (ihtibas) is broken — travel breaks the condition, but prayer and fasting do not.

In classical Hanafi law, a wife's right to maintenance (nafaqah) is conditional upon her being available for the husband's custody (ihtibas). This lesson examines a specific scenario: what happens to maintenance when the wife performs hajj without her husband? The passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the ruling and highlights an important disagreement within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its effect on maintenance
The wife performs hajj without her husband. The ruling is that maintenance lapses.
2
Understand the rationale
The loss of maintenance is due to the wife's own action of breaking custody (ihtibas).
3
Locate the proof-by-differentiation
The author contrasts hajj with prayer and fasting – those do not affect maintenance because custody remains intact.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that if the hajj is obligatory (Hajjat al-Islam), maintenance is retained because fulfilling a faridah is an excuse.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Zahir al-Riwayah (no maintenance) is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا حجت مع غير الزوج فلأن فوات الاحتباس منها . . وعن أبي يوسف أن لها النفقة لأن إقامة الفرض عذر فيكون لها نفقة الحضر. وفي رواية عنه يؤمر الزوج بالخروج معها والإنفاق عليها إذا أرادت حجة الإسلام؛ الذخيرة. أطلق الحج فشمل الفرض والنفل وما إذا حجت قبل أن تسلم نفسها أو بعده وهذا ظاهر الرواية لأن الامتناع من جهتها فأوجب سقوطها، سواء كانت عاصية في الخروج أو طائعة بخلاف الصلاة والصوم لوجود الاحتباس فلا يمنع اشتغالها بهما من وجوب النفقة؛ تحبس هو كذا في الذخيرة.
As for if she performs hajj with someone other than the husband, then because the loss of custody is from her. And from Abu Yusuf that she has maintenance because fulfilling the obligatory duty is an excuse, so she has maintenance of residence (nafaqat al-hadar). And in a narration from him: the husband is ordered to go out with her and spend on her if she wants the hajj of Islam. Al-Dhakhira. He made hajj absolute, so it includes obligatory and supererogatory, and whether she performs hajj before surrendering herself or after. And this is the apparent riwaya because the refusal is from her side, so it obligates its lapse, whether she is disobedient in going out or obedient, contrary to prayer and fasting because custody exists, so her engagement in them does not prevent the obligation of maintenance.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of when a wife's maintenance is affected by her own actions. If she performs hajj with a non-mahram or without her husband, she loses maintenance because the loss of ihtibas (custody) is attributable to her. The apparent riwaya (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that she has no maintenance, whether the hajj is obligatory or supererogatory, and whether she performed it before or after surrendering herself to the husband. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that she does receive maintenance if it is the obligatory hajj (Hajjat al-Islam), because fulfilling a faridah is an excuse. In one narration, he even said the husband should be ordered to accompany her and spend on her. The passage contrasts this with prayer and fasting: these do not remove maintenance because custody remains intact—she can pray and fast in the husband's house. But hajj requires travel, thus breaks custody.

Key Terms
نفقة الحضر (nafaqat al-hadar): Maintenance calculated as if the wife were residing in her hometown, not during travel.
حجة الإسلام (Hajjat al-Islam): The obligatory pilgrimage due once in a lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling on a wife's maintenance if she performs the obligatory Hajj without her husband?
A) She loses maintenance because the loss of custody is from her side.
B) She retains maintenance because it is a religious duty.
C) She loses maintenance only if the Hajj is supererogatory.
D) She retains maintenance but must repay it later.

Key Takeaway
A wife's maintenance lapses if she travels for hajj without her husband, because the condition of ihtibas (custody) is broken — this applies to all hajj, regardless of obligation.

Maintenance for the Sick Wife Before Consummation: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on maintenance for a sick wife before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance for a sick wife before consummation and explain the condition of ability to transfer.

Core Idea
A sick wife willing to transfer but unable still receives maintenance because taslim is achieved through istimta'.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between a wife who refuses to submit (nushuz) and one who is incapacitated by illness. This passage from Bahar al-Ra'iq resolves a seeming contradiction in the texts and establishes the mufta bihi: maintenance is due to the sick wife as long as she is willing to surrender and able to transfer. Understanding this ruling prevents wrongful denial of maintenance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Maintenance (nafaqah) for a wife who falls ill before consummation and before moving to the husband's house. The ruling: wajib under certain conditions.
The act is the wife's entitlement to maintenance, not a physical act.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the analogy (qiyas) to menstruating, postpartum, and fasting women: even though intercourse is not possible, istimta' (enjoyment) is possible, so taslim is achieved.
This analogy shows that taslim does not require actual intercourse.
3
Distinguish the positions
The apparent riwaya (Zahir al-Riwayah) grants maintenance if the wife does not refuse. Abu Yusuf holds no maintenance before transfer. Identify which is mufta bihi.
The later mashayikh (e.g., in Fath al-Qadir) authenticate the apparent riwaya with the added condition of ability to transfer.
4
Analyse the condition of ability to transfer
The passage states that if the wife cannot transfer at all (e.g., bedridden), then maintenance is not due because taslim is entirely lacking.
This condition reconciles the texts: only a wife who can transfer (even if not actually moved) is entitled.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the apparent riwaya with the condition of ability to transfer: maintenance is wajib if the wife is willing and able to move.
This is the fatwa according to Fath al-Qadir, al-Bada'i', and others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المريضة التي لم تزف فالمراد بها المريضة التي لم تنتقل إلى بيت الزوج، وقد اختلفت عبارات الكتب في هذه المسألة فظاهر المختصر أنها إذا مرضت قبل الدخول وهي في غير بيت الزوج فإنه لا نفقة لها، ومفهومه أنها إن كانت في بيته فلها النفقة. وعلى هذا فالفرق بينها وبين الصحيحة إنما هو من جهة أن الصحيحة إذا لم تمنع نفسها من الانتقال مع الزوج فلها النفقة طلبها الزوج أو لا بخلاف المريضة فإنه لا نفقة لها وهي في بيتها مطلقاً. وفي البدائع ما يخالفه فإنه قال : لو كانت المرأة مريضة قبل النقلة مرضاً يمنع من الجماع فنقلت وهي مريضة فلها النفقة بعد النقلة وقبلها أيضاً إذا طلبت النفقة فلم ينقلها الزوج وهي لا تمتنع من النقلة لو طالبها الزوج وإن كانت تمتنع فلا نفقة لها كالصحيحة؛ كذا ذكره في ظاهر الرواية. وروي عن أبي يوسف أنه لا نفقة لها قبل النقلة فإذا نقلت وهي مريضة فله أن يردها وجه ظاهر الرواية أن التسليم في حق التمكين من الوطء إن لم يوجد فقد وجد في حق التمكين من الاستمتاع وهذا يكفي لوجوب النفقة كما في الحائض والنفساء والصائمة صوم رمضان، وإذا امتنعت لم يوجد التسليم شرعاً ا فحاصله أن ظاهر الرواية أن المريضة كالصحيحة فلا ينبغي ادخالها في النساء اللاتي لا نفقة لهن. وفي التجنيس : المرأة قبل الدخول بها إذا مرضت وطلبت النفقة يفرض لها النفقة إن لم يكن يحول بينه وبين أن يضمها إليه لأنها ما امتنعت من تسليم النفس، وإن امتنعت من ذلك فلا نفقة عليه ا هـ . وظاهره أنه إذا كان مرضها مانعاً من النقلة فلا نفقة لها وإن لم تمنع نفسها وعليه يحمل ما في المختصر . وحاصله أن المنقول في ظاهر الرواية النفقة للمريضة، سواء كان قبل النقلة أو بعدها، وسواء كان يمكنه جماعها أو لا، كان معها زوجها أو لا، حيث لم تمنع نفسها كما صرح به في البدائع والخلاصة والذخيرة وغاية البيان معزياً إلى كافي الحاكم والمبسوط والشامل وشرح الطحاوي فكان هو المذهب، وصححه في فتح القدير وقال : إن الفتوى عليه وذكر أن القائلين بعدم فرعوه على اشتراط التسليم حقيقة وهو مروي عن أبي يوسف وليس هو المختار والذي ظهر لي أن ما ذكره المشايخ إنما هو ظاهر الرواية لا أنه مفرع على رواية أبي يوسف فإن النفقة وإن كانت واجبة للمريضة في ظاهر الرواية قبل الانتقال حيث لم تمنع نفسها لكن بشرط أن يمكنها الانتقال، فلو كانت بحيث لا يمكنها الانتقال أصلاً فلا نفقة لها لعدم التسليم تقديراً بدليل قولهم في توجيه ظاهر الرواية أن التسليم حاصل في حق التمكين من الاستمتاع وإن لم يكن انتقالها فات التسليم بالكلية، فهذا هو مراد الفارقين بين المريضة ،والصحيحة، فالمريضة التي لم تزف
As for the sick woman who has not been handed over (i.e., not yet moved), what is meant is the sick woman who has not transferred to the husband's house. The expressions of the books differ on this issue: the literal reading of al-Mukhtar is that if she falls sick before consummation while not in the husband's house, she has no maintenance; its implication is that if she is in his house, she does have maintenance. On this basis, the difference between her and a healthy woman is only that a healthy woman who does not prevent herself from transferring to the husband gets maintenance whether he asks or not, contrary to the sick woman who has no maintenance at all while in her own house. In al-Bada'i', something contradictory: he said if the woman is sick before transfer with a sickness preventing intercourse, and she transfers while sick, she gets maintenance after transfer and also before it if she requested maintenance but the husband did not transfer her, and she is not preventing transfer had the husband demanded; if she does prevent, then no maintenance like a healthy woman. Thus mentioned in the apparent riwaya. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that she has no maintenance before transfer; if she transfers while sick, he can return her. The face of the apparent riwaya is that submission (taslim) regarding the ability to have intercourse, if not found, has been found regarding the ability to enjoy (istimta'), and that suffices for wajib maintenance, as in the case of menstruating, postpartum, and fasting in Ramadan. If she refrains, then submission is not found legally. So the summary is that the apparent riwaya treats the sick woman like the healthy woman, so she should not be included among women who have no maintenance. In al-Tajnis: the woman before consummation, if she falls sick and requests maintenance, maintenance is prescribed for her if there is no obstacle preventing him from bringing her to him, because she has not refrained from surrendering herself; if she refrains, then no maintenance. The apparent meaning is that if her sickness prevents transfer, then no maintenance even if she does not refrain. On this is based what is in al-Mukhtar. The summary: what is transmitted in the apparent riwaya is maintenance for the sick woman, whether before or after transfer, whether he can have intercourse with her or not, whether her husband is with her or not, as long as she does not refrain from surrendering herself. This is the madhhab, and it is authenticated in Fath al-Qadir, who said the fatwa is upon it, and mentioned that those who deny it base it on the condition of actual submission, which is narrated from Abu Yusuf and is not the chosen view. What appears to me is that what the mashayikh mentioned is the apparent riwaya, not based on Abu Yusuf's narration, because maintenance, though wajib for the sick woman in the apparent riwaya before transfer as long as she does not refrain, is conditional upon her ability to transfer. If she cannot transfer at all, then no maintenance due to lack of submission consideratively, as evidenced by their statement in explaining the apparent riwaya: submission is achieved regarding the ability to enjoy (istimta'), but if transfer is completely impossible, then submission is entirely lacking. This is the intended meaning of those who distinguish between the sick and the healthy woman. So the sick woman who has not been handed over...
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This extended passage from Bahar al-Ra'iq resolves a seeming contradiction within the Hanafi school regarding a wife who falls ill before consummation and before moving into the husband's house. The issue: does she receive maintenance? Al-Mukhtar (matn) suggests she does not, because she has not fully surrendered. But al-Bada'i' and others report a different ruling in the 'apparent riwaya' (Zahir al-Riwayah): she does get maintenance as long as she does not actively refuse to transfer to him. The key distinction: the healthy wife is obligated to move when asked; if she doesn't, she loses maintenance. The sick wife, if she is willing to move but her sickness prevents it, still gets maintenance because she is not refusing (nushuz). However, if her sickness prevents transfer entirely (e.g., bedridden), then she loses maintenance because submission (taslim) is impossible even legally (taqdiran). The commentator synthesizes: the madhhab (mufta bihi) is that maintenance is due to the sick wife if she is willing and able to transfer; if she is physically unable, she has no maintenance. This reconciles the texts. Abu Yusuf held that maintenance is not due before transfer, but the relied-upon position is the apparent riwaya as explained.

Key Terms
التسليم (al-taslim): The wife's legal submission to the husband, which includes being available for his legitimate enjoyment (istimta'), even if intercourse is not possible due to illness.
الاستمتاع (al-istimta'): The right of the husband to enjoy his wife in permissible ways short of intercourse (e.g., looking, touching).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view (mufta bihi), does a sick woman who has not yet moved to her husband's house receive maintenance?
A) Yes, as long as she does not refuse to surrender and is able to transfer.
B) No, because she has not submitted completely.
C) Yes, unconditionally regardless of ability to move.
D) No, only if the husband demands she come.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi awards maintenance to the sick wife before consummation if she does not refuse surrender and is physically able to transfer.

The Obligation of Providing a Servant for the Wife: Ownership Requirement in Zahir al-Riwayah
Explains the obligation of a servant for the wife and the condition of ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on providing a servant for the wife and explain the condition of ownership according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
A husband must provide for his wife's servant only if the servant is her property.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key detail in the wife's maintenance (nafaqah): the servant (khadim). While the husband is obligated to maintain his wife, the extent of that maintenance includes a servant only under certain conditions. The strongest transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) ties the obligation to the wife's ownership of the servant, a point that resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding this condition prevents misapplication of the nafaqah rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
The passage begins by stating that for a wealthy husband (muwsir), maintenance and clothing for the wife's servant are wajib. This is part of completing her maintenance.
The ruling applies only if the husband is financially able.
2
Note the conditions for obligation
Besides the husband's wealth, the servant must be devoted to the wife's service (not occupied elsewhere). The minimum sufficiency is provided, not the same level as the wife's maintenance.
The condition of devotion appears in al-Bada'i' and Sharh al-Tahawi.
3
Recognize the interpretive dispute
The author uses the term 'servant' absolutely, leading to disagreement. Some scholars include any server, free or slave, owned by anyone. Zahir al-Riwayah from the three imams restricts it to the wife's owned slave.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the Zahir al-Riwayah rule
If the wife does not own a servant, the husband is not obligated to provide for one. The entitlement arises from her ownership, not mere need.
Al-Dhakhira confirms this as the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والخادم لو موسراً) أي تجب النفقة والكسوة لخادم المرأة لأن كفايتها واجبة عليه وهذا من تمامه إذ لا بد لها منه فيلزمه للخادم أدنى الكفاية لا تبلغ نفقة المرأة، وكذا كسوته بأرخص ما يكون ويفرض للخادم خف لأنها تحتاج إلى الخروج بخلاف المرأة؛ كذا في الخانية. وفسر في الهداية نفقة الخادم بما يلزم المعسر من نفقة امرأته وشرط في البدائع وشرح الطحاوي في وجوب نفقة خادمها أن لا يكون له شغل غير خدمتها بأن يكون متفرغاً لها . وأطلق المصنف في الخادم ولم يضفه إليها للاختلاف في تفسيره فقيل هو كل من يخدمها حراً كان أو عبداً. ملكاً لها أو له أو لهما أو لغيرهما. وظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا الثلاثة كما في الذخيرة أنه مملوكها فلو لم يكن لها خادم لا يفرض عليه نفقة خادم لأنها بسبب ملكها له فإذا أما على ظاهر الرواية من اشتراط كون الخادم بمملوكاً لها فلا فإنه إذا لم يكن مملوكاً لها لا نفقة له على الزوج وإن كانت محتاجة إليه كما يعلم من قول المؤلف وأطلق المصنف في الخادم الخ» تأمل قوله : (وظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا الثلاثة (الخ عبارة الذخيرة هكذا قال وإن لم يكن للمرأة خادم لا يفرض نفقة الخادم على الزوج في ظاهر الرواية عن أصحابنا الثلاثة لأن استحقاقها نفقة الخادم باعتبار ملك الخادم، فإذا لم يكن لها خادم كيف تستوجب نفقة الخادم وهو نظير القاضي الخ. أقول: وهذه العبارة ليست نصاً في اشتراط كون الخادم ملكاً لها قوله : فيه نظر) قال الرملي: لو قال فيه قصور
His saying: (And the servant, if he is wealthy) means maintenance and clothing are obligatory for the wife's servant because her maintenance is obligatory upon him, and this is part of its completion since she inevitably needs him. So he must provide for the servant the minimum sufficiency, not reaching the wife's maintenance, and similarly his clothing at the cheapest rate. And a light shoe is prescribed for the servant because she needs to go out, unlike the wife. Thus in al-Khaniyya. And in al-Hidaya, the maintenance of the servant is interpreted as what is required for the impoverished husband for his wife's maintenance. And in al-Bada'i' and Sharh al-Tahawi, it is conditioned for the obligation of the servant's maintenance that he has no occupation other than serving her, i.e., he must be devoted to her. And the author used the term 'servant' in absolute sense and did not attribute it to her, due to difference in its interpretation. So it is said: It is every one who serves her, free or slave, owned by her, him, both, or others. And Zahir al-Riwayah from our three imams, as in al-Dhakhira, is that it is her owned property. So if she has no servant, he is not required to pay maintenance for a servant, because her entitlement is due to her ownership of the servant. Then, on the basis of Zahir al-Riwayah of the condition that the servant is her property, if it is not her property, there is no maintenance upon the husband even if she needs it, as understood from the author's statement: 'And the author used the term servant absolutely...' Consider his saying: (And Zahir al-Riwayah from our three imams...) The expression of al-Dhakhira is as follows: 'If the woman has no servant, maintenance of the servant is not prescribed upon the husband in Zahir al-Riwayah from our three imams, because her entitlement to maintenance of the servant is based on ownership of the servant. So if she has no servant, how can she become entitled to maintenance of the servant? And it is analogous to the qadi, etc.' I say: This expression is not explicit in stipulating that the servant is her property. His saying: 'There is consideration in it.' Al-Ramli said: If he said 'there is deficiency in it'.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation of the husband to provide a servant for his wife as part of her maintenance (nafaqah). The author explains that if the husband is wealthy, he must provide a servant for his wife because she needs assistance. The minimum level of maintenance for the servant is described: basic food, clothing, and shoes suitable for going out. There is a condition in some sources that the servant must be exclusively devoted to the wife's service. The key point of disagreement is the interpretation of 'servant' (khadim). Some scholars include any person who serves her, regardless of ownership. However, according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the strongest transmission from the three senior imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad), the servant must be the wife's own property (mamluk). If she does not own a servant, the husband is not obligated to provide one because her right to a servant is based on ownership. The author concludes by noting that the expression in al-Dhakhira is not explicit on this condition, and al-Ramli criticizes it as insufficient.

Key Terms
الخادم (al-khadim): The servant who serves the wife. In this context, the term is ambiguous: some include any server, others restrict to the wife's owned slave.
كفايتها (kifayatuha): The wife's maintenance, which includes food, clothing, and necessary assistance such as a servant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah in this passage, when is a husband obligated to pay maintenance for a servant for his wife?
A) Whenever the wife needs a servant, regardless of ownership.
B) Only if the wife owns a servant who serves her.
C) Only if the husband is wealthy and the servant is free.
D) Only if the couple lives in a large house.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, a husband is only obligated to provide maintenance for his wife's servant if the servant is her property; mere need does not create the obligation.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate
12 min
Providing a Servant to the Wife: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on providing a servant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on providing a servant to the wife, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of servants, and apply the mufta bihi position based on the wife's status and the husband's wealth.

Core Idea
The husband must provide a servant if the wife owns none; the number depends on her need, with the later view allowing more than one.

The maintenance (nafaqah) of a wife extends to providing a servant (khādim) if she needs one. However, the Hanafi school has internal differences on how many servants are obligatory. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the key dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) over the number, and how later scholars adopted Abu Yusuf's view, making it the operative fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
The husband is obligated (wajib) to provide a servant for the wife, but only if she does not already own one. If she owns one, he must maintain it. If not, he is not required to hire one but must purchase necessities.
The servant must be owned by the wife; the husband cannot force his own servant on her.
2
Analyze the dispute on number of servants
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: one servant suffices. Abu Yusuf initially said two servants (one for internal tasks, one for external), and in another narration, more if needed for high-status women.
The dispute is recorded in zahir al-riwayah; later scholars weighed the evidence.
3
Understand the tarjih (preponderance)
Later Hanafi masters (e.g., al-Tahawi, authors of al-Hidayah) adopted Abu Yusuf's view, making the number dependent on the wife's status and need. This is now the mufta bihi position.
‘Status’ (ḥāl) refers to her social standing and prior lifestyle in her father’s house.
4
Examine conditions and exceptions
The husband must be wealthy (yāsir); if poor, the obligation drops. Also, a slave wife does not deserve a servant's maintenance. The obligation is only for a servant owned by the wife.
If the wife refuses to let her own servant serve her, the husband must still provide maintenance for the servant.
5
Distinguish legal enforceability from religious duty
Some tasks (cooking, baking) are religiously obligatory (dīyānatan) but not legally enforceable (qadā'an). The same distinction applies to the servant's maintenance: the court may not force a poor husband, but he is still accountable before Allah.
This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh for understanding the limits of judicial intervention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

البيان أن الخادم واحد ،الخدام غلاماً ما كان أو جارية. وبه تبين أن تفسير الزيلعي خادمها بالجارية المملوكة لها في ظاهر الرواية فيه نظر، وينبغي أن يدخل المدبر والمدبرة تحته . وبهذا علم أنه إذا لم يكن لها لم تطبخ لا يعطيها الإدام وهو الصحيح وقالوا إن هذه الأعمال واجبة عليها ديانة وإن كان لا يجبرها القاضي ا هـ. ولذا قال في البدائع : لو استأجرها للطبخ والخبز لم يجز ولا يجوز لها أخذ الأجرة على ذلك لأنها لو أخذت لأخذت على عمل واجب عليها في الفتوى فكان في معنى الرشوة فلا يحل لها الأخذا هـ. وهو شامل لبنات الأشراف أيضاً ولذا استدل في البدائع لوجوبه ديانة بأنه عليه السلام قسم الأعمال بين علي وفاطمة فجعل أعمال الخارج على علي وأعمال الداخل على فاطمة ا هـ . مع أنها سيدة نساء العالمين رضي الله تعالى عنها وأبوها صلى الله عليه وسلم أفضل الخلق أجمعين. وقيد بيسار الزوج لأنه لا يجب عليه نفقة الخادم عند إعساره وهو رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة وهو الأصح خلافاً لما قاله محمد لأن الواجب على المعسر أدنى الكفاية . تكتفي بخدمة نفسها كذا في الهداية. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه مخالف لما ذكره أولاً من لزوم اعتبار حالهما وأنه عند إعساره دونها ينفق بقدر حاله والباقي دين عليه، وقياسه أن تجب النفقة للخادم ديناً عليه ا.هـ. وقد يقال إنما قيل في نفقتها ذلك للجمع بين الدليلين الآية وحديث هند وليس ذلك في الخادم فبقي على الأصل من اعتبار حاله. وفي الذخيرة : ولا تقدر نفقة الخادم بالدراهم على ما ذكرنا في نفقة المرأة بل يفرض لها ما يكفيها بالمعروف ولكن لا تبلغ نفقة خادمها نفقتها لأن الخادم تبع للمرأة فتنقص نفقة الخادم عن نفقتها، ولم يرد بالنقصان النقصان في الخبز لأن النفقة بقدر الكفاية وعسى . أن تستوفي الخادم من الخبز في الأكل أكثر مما تستوفي ،المرأة، وإنما أراد به النقصان في الإدام ا هـ. وفيها أيضاً : والكسوة للخادم على المعسر قميص كرباس في الشتاء وإزار ورداء كأرخص ما يكون، وفي خدمك ولكن أعطي . خادماً من خدمي ليخدمك فأبت المرأة لم يكن للزوج ذلك ويجبر على نفقة خادم واحد من خدام المرأة ا هـ من التتارخانية أقول : فأشار بقوله بنت فائق» إلى أن المعتبر حالها في بيت أبيها لا حالها الطارئ عليها في بيت الزوج تأمل ا هـ قوله : (قال) الفقيه أبو الليث الخ) في البدائع : وذكر الفقيه أبو الليث أنها إذا كانت بها علة لا تقدر على الطبخ والخبز أو كانت من بنات الأشراف لا تجبر، فأما إذا كانت تقدر على ذلك وهي ممن تخدم نفسها تجبر على ذلك ا هـ.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Maintenance. If she does not possess [a servant], he is not obligated to provide its maintenance, like the judge who does not have a servant does not deserve the servant's maintenance from the treasury. The apparent meaning of their statement is that her servant is that which is owned by her, whether a male slave or a female slave. For this reason, it is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that the servant is one, whether slave or maid. By this it becomes clear that the interpretation of al-Zayla'i that her servant is the female slave owned by her in the apparent narration is questionable, and it should include the mudabbar and mudabbara [slaves whose freedom is deferred]. From this it is known that if she does not own a servant, the husband is not obligated to hire a slave to serve her, but he is obligated to buy for her what she needs from the market, as explicitly stated in al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyya. It is restricted to the servant because he is not obligated to provide maintenance for more than one servant for her, and this is according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. Abu Yusuf said: He should assign two servants because she needs one for internal tasks and another for external tasks. The two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: One person can do both tasks, so there is no need for two. Al-Tahawi said: The author of al-Imla narrated from Abu Yusuf that if the woman is of such high status that one servant is insufficient, he should spend on as many servants as she cannot do without, whether more than one or more than two. He said: We take that position. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. In al-Zahiriyya and al-Walwalijiyya: If the woman is from the daughters of nobles and she has servants, the husband is forced to provide maintenance for two servants. The conclusion is that the madhhab is to limit to one absolutely, and the taken position among the later scholars is the statement of Abu Yusuf. In Fath al-Qadir and al-Dhakhira: If he has children and one servant is insufficient, he is required to provide two or more as needed, unanimously. In al-Tajnis: A woman had slaves and said to her husband, "Spend on them from my mahr," and he spent. Then she said, "I do not consider it from the mahr because you employed them." Whatever he spent in a reasonable manner is counted against her because it was by her order. The obligation of the servant's maintenance is absolute, so it includes if the husband wants to serve her himself or have his own servant serve her, he does not spend on her servant. He said in al-Khaniyya: If the husband says, "I will serve you" or "a female slave from my female slaves will serve you," the correct view is that the husband does not have the right to evict the wife's servant from his house. Al-Walwaliji explained it because the woman may not find service with the husband's service. Its apparent meaning is that he has the right to evict more than one servant from his house because it is extra to the statement of the two. It is absolute regarding the woman, so it includes the slave woman and the free noble and lowly, but in al-Khulasa, attributed to al-Fatawa al-Sughra: If the married woman is a slave, she does not deserve the servant's maintenance; the servant's maintenance is for the daughters of nobles. It is inconceivable for a slave woman to have a servant in the apparent narration because it is owned by the woman, and the slave has no ownership. Rather, it is according to the one who interpreted the servant as any servant owned or not. Some have taken what is in al-Khulasa that if she is of the lowly, she does not deserve maintenance. It would be more appropriate that it is answered that it is based on the common practice that women take servants from the category of slave girls, not that it is a restriction. Consider his statement: "Abu Yusuf said: He should assign two servants," etc. Al-Ramli said: I say: And from Abu Yusuf in another narration, i.e., other than the narration of two servants, that if the woman is of high status, the daughter of high status, and she is brought to her husband's house with many servants, she deserves the maintenance of all the servants from the husband. If the husband says to his wife, "I will not spend on any of the servants," even if she is free because he restricted it to the daughters of nobles. He said in Fath al-Qadir: It is supported by what the faqih Abu al-Layth restricted in the statement of al-Khassaf, where he said in Adab al-Qadi: If he assigned what she needs of flour, oil, meat, and condiments, and she said, "I will not knead, nor bake, nor handle anything of that," she is not forced to do so, and the husband must bring someone who suffices for that work. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: This is if she has an illness that prevents her from cooking and baking, or if she is not one who does that. If she is one who serves herself and is able to do that, he is not obligated to bring someone to do it. In some places, she is forced to do that. Al-Sarakhsi said: She is not forced, but if she does not cook, he does not give her the oil, and that is the correct view. They said: These tasks are obligatory upon her religiously, even if the judge does not force her. Therefore, it is said in al-Bada'i: If he hires her for cooking and baking, it is not valid, and it is not permissible for her to take wages for that because if she took wages, she would be taking payment for an act that is obligatory upon her in religious verdicts, so it is like a bribe, so it is not permissible for her to take it. This includes the daughters of nobles as well. For this reason, in al-Bada'i, he used as evidence for its religious obligation that he (peace be upon him) divided the tasks between Ali and Fatima, so he made the external tasks for Ali and the internal tasks for Fatima, despite her being the chief of the women of the worlds (may Allah be pleased with her) and her father (peace be upon him) is the best of all creation. It is restricted by the husband's wealth because the servant's maintenance is not obligatory upon him when he is poor, and this is the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa, and it is the most correct, contrary to what Muhammad said because the obligation upon the poor is the minimum sufficiency. She serves herself as in al-Hidaya. In Fath al-Qadir, he objected to it that it contradicts what he first mentioned about the necessity of considering both states, and that when he is poor and she is not, he spends according to his state and the rest is a debt upon him, and its analog would be that the servant's maintenance is a debt upon him. It may be said that this is said in her maintenance to reconcile between the two proofs—the verse and the hadith of Hind—and that is not the case with the servant, so it remains on the principle of considering his state. In al-Dhakhira: The servant's maintenance is not assessed in dirhams as we mentioned in the woman's maintenance; rather, sufficient is assigned for her in a reasonable manner, but the servant's maintenance does not reach the woman's maintenance because the servant is dependent on the woman, so the servant's maintenance is less than her maintenance. By less, he did not mean less in bread because maintenance is according to sufficiency, and it is possible that the servant takes more bread in eating than the woman takes; rather, he meant less in condiments. In it also: The clothing for the servant for the poor husband: a cotton shirt in winter, a waist-wrapper, and a cloak at the cheapest. And in "And I will serve you, but I give a servant from my servants to serve you" and the woman refused, the husband does not have that, and he is forced to provide maintenance for one servant from the wife's servants. From al-Tatar Khaniyya. He (al-Ramli) said: He indicated by his statement "daughter of high status" that what matters is her state in her father's house, not the state that has come upon her in the husband's house; consider. His statement: "The faqih Abu al-Layth said" etc. In al-Bada'i: Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned that if she has an illness that prevents her from cooking and baking, or if she is from the daughters of nobles, she is not forced. But if she is able to do that and she is one who serves herself, she is forced to do that.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq, addresses the obligation of a husband to provide a servant (khādim) for his wife. The discussion begins by clarifying that the servant must be owned by the wife; if she does not own one, the husband is not required to hire a servant but must purchase necessary items. The key dispute is over the number of servants: according to the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad), only one servant is obligatory, while Abū Yūsuf (in another view) requires two for internal and external tasks. However, later scholars like al-Ṭaḥāwī adopt the position that more than one may be required based on the wife's status. The relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) among later scholars is that of Abū Yūsuf, allowing for more than one if needed. The passage also covers other scenarios: the husband cannot force his own servant on the wife; a slave wife does not deserve a servant's maintenance; the obligation of domestic work (cooking, baking) is religiously binding but not legally enforceable; and the condition of the husband's wealth—if poor, he is not obligated to provide a servant. The text also includes details on the quantity and quality of the servant's maintenance and clothing.

Key Terms
خادم (khādim): A servant (male or female) owned by the wife, used for her service.
نفقة الخادم (nafaqat al-khādim): The maintenance (food, clothing, etc.) of the wife's servant, which the husband must provide if she needs it.
ديانة (dīyānatan): Religiously obligatory, meaning the wife is accountable before Allah even if the court does not enforce it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which position is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) among later Hanafi scholars regarding the number of servants a husband must provide for his wife?
A) Exactly one servant, regardless of the wife's status.
B) Two servants, one for internal tasks and one for external tasks.
C) As many servants as the wife's need and status require, potentially more than one.
D) No servant is required if the husband serves her himself.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on providing a servant is wajib, with the number of servants depending on the wife's status and need, and the mufta bihi view allows for more than one.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate

The Obligation to Provide a Servant for the Wife
Ruling on when husband must provide servant, with conditions and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi husband must provide a servant for his wife and identify the relied-upon position in the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A husband must provide a servant only if the wife is from a noble family or unable to work, and he is wealthy.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on providing a servant (khadim) for the wife. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the conditions based on the wife's social status and the husband's financial ability, and discusses an internal disagreement within the school. The ruling is supported by the hadith of the division of work between Ali and Fatima.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
The passage states that the husband must provide a servant (wajib) if the wife is from a noble family (banat al-ashraf) or has an illness preventing her from doing household work, and the husband is wealthy (yasar).
The ruling is a religious obligation (diyanatan) but not enforceable by the judge.
2
Analyze the primary proof
The author cites the hadith where the Prophet divided work between Ali (outside) and Fatima (inside), indicating that even Fatima performed indoor work, but the implication is that women of her status are not required to do heavy labor. This proves that if the wife is from a high-status family, the husband must provide a servant.
The hadith is used to show that domestic work is not inherently obligatory on the wife.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text presents an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa (via Hasan) holds that if the husband is poor, he is not obligated to provide a servant. Muhammad holds that even the poor must provide minimum sufficiency. Abu Yusuf's view is not mentioned.
The relied-upon (al-ashahh) position is that of Abu Hanifa.
4
Understand the tarjih reasoning
Fath al-Qadir critiques the reasoning behind the opposition, but the author defends Abu Hanifa's view by distinguishing the wife's own maintenance (which can become a debt) from the servant's maintenance (which remains on the principle of considering the husband's current ability).
The distinction is based on combining two proofs for the wife's maintenance versus the original principle for the servant.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a husband is wealthy and his wife is from a noble family or has a valid excuse, he must hire a servant for her. If he is poor, he is not required to do so, and the wife must serve herself.
The judge does not enforce this, but it is a religious duty.

الخادم وإن كانت حرة لأنه قيدها ببنات الأشراف . قال في فتح القدير: ويوافقه ما قيد به الفقيه أبو الليث كلام الخصاف حيث قال في أدب القاضي : لو فرض ما يحتاج إليه من الدقيق والدهن واللحم والإدام فقالت لا أعجن ولا أخبز ولا أعالج شيئاً من ذلك لا تجبر عليه وعلى الزوج أن يأتيها بمن يكفيها عمل ذلك .

السرخسي : لا تجبر ولكن إذا لم تطبخ لا يعطيها الإدام وهو الصحيح وقالوا إن هذه الأعمال واجبة عليها ديانة وإن كان لا يجبرها القاضي ا هـ. ولذا قال في البدائع : لو استأجرها للطبخ والخبز لم يجز ولا يجوز لها أخذ الأجرة على ذلك لأنها لو أخذت لأخذت على عمل واجب عليها في الفتوى فكان في معنى الرشوة فلا يحل لها الأخذا هـ. وهو شامل لبنات الأشراف أيضاً ولذا استدل في البدائع لوجوبه ديانة بأنه عليه السلام قسم Book of Divorce, Chapter of Maintenance. The servant, even if she is free, because he restricted it to daughters of nobles. He said in Fath al-Qadir: And it agrees with what al-Faqih Abu al-Layth restricted in the speech of al-Khassaf, where he said in Adab al-Qadi: If one prescribes what is needed of flour, oil, meat, and condiment, and she says, 'I will not knead, nor bake, nor prepare anything of that,' she is not compelled to do so, and the husband must bring someone who suffices her in that work. ...
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the husband's obligation to provide a servant for his wife. The author begins by stating that the husband must provide a servant if the wife is from the nobility (banat al-ashraf). He cites al-Fath al-Qadir agreeing with al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, who in Adab al-Qadi rules that if the husband provides ingredients but the wife refuses to prepare them, she is not compelled to work and the husband must hire someone. Abu al-Layth qualifies this: if the wife has a reason preventing her from cooking (e.g., illness) or if she is from a family that does not do such work, she is not compelled; but if she is capable and normally serves herself, the husband is not obliged to hire a servant, and in some places she is compelled. Al-Sarakhsi holds that she is not compelled, but if she does not cook, she does not receive the condiment; this is the sahih view. The scholars say these duties are wajib upon her in religious terms (diyanatan), even if the judge does not enforce them. Al-Bada'i' adds that hiring her for cooking is invalid, and she may not take wages for such work, as it is obligatory and taking wages would be akin to bribery. This applies even to noblewomen, as evidenced by the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) divided household work between Ali (outside) and Fatima (inside), even though Fatima was the best of women. The ruling is restricted by the husband's wealth (yasar): he is not obligated for a servant's maintenance if he is poor (mu'sir). This is the riwayah of Hasan from Abu Hanifah, and it is the most sahih position, contrary to Muhammad's view that the poor must provide the minimum sufficiency. The author notes that in al-Hidayah it says the wife suffices with her own service. Fath al-Qadir critiques this as contradictory to earlier principles that both parties' circumstances are considered; if he is poor and she is not, he pays according to his ability and the remainder is a debt. The response is that the wife's maintenance is based on combining two proofs (Qur'an and hadith of Hind), whereas the servant's maintenance remains on the original principle of considering his ability. In al-Dhakhirah: the servant's maintenance is not set in dirhams like the wife's; rather, it is estimated by sufficiency (kifayah), but it does not reach the wife's level because the servant is subordinate. The reduction is not in bread (since both eat according to need) but in condiment. Also, the clothing for the servant: for the poor husband, a cotton shirt in winter and a waist wrapper and garment as cheap as possible; for the wealthy, similar but better quality. The servant is not given a khimar (headcover) because her head is not 'awrah, unlike the wife. The author notes that these details are based on custom and vary by time and place. The passage ends with a remark that the criterion is the wife's state in her father's home, not her acquired state in the husband's home.

Key Terms
الخادم (al-khadim): A servant (female) provided by the husband for the wife's domestic work, such as cooking and cleaning.
يسار (yasar): Wealth or financial ability; the threshold for being considered wealthy enough to be obliged to provide a servant.
إعسار (i'sar): Poverty; being unable to afford a servant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is a husband obliged to provide a servant for his wife?
A) Whenever the wife requests one, regardless of her ability to work.
B) Only if the wife is from a noble family or has a valid reason preventing her from doing the work, and the husband is wealthy.
C) Only if the husband is poor, because then the wife must hire a servant herself.
D) Always, because household work is not the wife's duty.

Key Takeaway
Providing a servant for the wife is wajib when she is from a noble family or unable to work, provided the husband is wealthy; internal school difference on the poor husband is resolved with Abu Hanifa's view.

Maintenance and Clothing for the Servant
Rulings on servant maintenance and clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the maintenance obligation for a wife from that of a servant in Hanafi fiqh and identify the clothing requirements for a female servant.

Core Idea
A servant's maintenance is conditional upon service; her covering is reduced because her head is not 'awrah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the specific rulings for maintaining and clothing a female servant. While the husband is obligated to provide, this obligation is fundamentally different from the wife's—it is an exchange for her domestic work. The passage also clarifies which garments are required and why the servant does not need a khimar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of maintenance
Recognize that the passage compares wife and servant maintenance. Wife's maintenance is in exchange for confinement (ihtibas); servant's is in exchange for service.
2
Examine clothing prescriptions
Note the specific garments for the servant in different seasons and wealth levels. Understand why the khimar is not prescribed (head not 'awrah) but the izar is (needs to go out).
3
Understand yasar and evidence rules
Define yasar as the nisab that prevents charity, not zakat. Learn the rules of evidence when husband and wife dispute over wealth: husband's word unless wife proves, and if both prove, wife's evidence is preferred.
4
Analyze the condition for servant's maintenance
Realize that the servant's maintenance is conditional on her work. If she refuses domestic tasks, she forfeits maintenance, unlike the wife.
