الصيف قميص مثل ذلك وإزار وعلى الموسر في الشتاء قميص وطىء وإزار كرياس وكساء رخيص، وفي الصيف قميص مثل ذلك وإزار . ثم لم يفرض للخادمة الخمار وفرضها للمرأة لأن الخمار لستر الرأس ورأس المرأة عورة ورأس الخادم ليس بعورة، وفرض لها الإزار لأن الخادم تحتاج إلى الخروج قال :مشايخنا ما ذكره محمد في الكتاب من ثياب الخادم فهو بناء على عاداتهم وذلك يختلف باختلاف الأمكنة في شدة الحر والبرد باختلاف العادات في كل وقت، فعلى القاضي اعتبار الكفاية في نفقة الخادم فيما يفرض في كل وقت ومكان ا هـ . وما ذكره من كسوة الخادم على المعسر إنما هو على قول محمد كما لا يخفى. وفي غاية البيان : واليسار مقدر بنصاب حرمان الصدقة لا بنصاب وجوب الزكاة ا هـ . وإن اختلفا في اليسار والإعسار فالقول قوله إلا أن تقيم المرأة البيئة ويشترط العدد والعدالة في هذا الخبر ولا يشترط لفظة الشهادة، وإن أقاما البينة فبيئتها أولى؛ كذا في الخانية . ثم اعلم أن نفقة الخادم إنما تجب على الزوج بإزاء الخدمة فإن امتنعت من الطبخ والخبز وأعمال البيت لم تستحق النفقة لأنه لم يوجد ما تستحق النفقة بمقابلتها بخلاف نفقة المرأة فإنها في مقابلة الاحتباس، فإذا لم تعمل تستحق النفقة وهذا هو ظاهر الرواية؛ كذا في الذخيرة .
In summer, a shirt like that and a waist-wrapper; and for the wealthy in winter, a shirt and a worn garment, a cotton waist-wrapper, and a cheap cloak; and in summer, a shirt like that and a waist-wrapper. Then, the khimar (headcover) was not prescribed for the female servant, but it was prescribed for the wife, because the khimar is for covering the head, and the wife's head is 'awrah, while the servant's head is not 'awrah. And the izar was prescribed for her because the servant needs to go out. Our mashayikh said: What Muhammad mentioned in the book about the servant's clothing is based on their customs, and that differs according to places in severe heat and cold, and according to customs in every time. So the judge must consider sufficiency in the servant's maintenance in what is prescribed in every time and place. End quote. And what he mentioned about the servant's clothing for the poor is only according to Muhammad's saying, as is not hidden. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: Wealth (yasar) is estimated by the nisab that prevents charity, not by the nisab that necessitates zakat. End quote. And if they differ about wealth and poverty, the word is his (the husband's), unless the woman establishes proof, and number and 'adalah are required in this testimony, and the wording 'shahadah' is not required. And if they both present evidence, her evidence is given precedence; thus in al-Khaniyyah. Then know that the servant's maintenance is only obligatory on the husband in exchange for service. If she refrains from cooking, baking, and household work, she is not entitled to maintenance, because there is no service against which to entitle her to maintenance, unlike the wife's maintenance which is in exchange for confinement (ihtibas). So if she does not work, she still is entitled to maintenance. This is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah); thus in al-Dhakhirah.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the specific rulings for the maintenance (nafaqah) and clothing (kiswah) of the servant (khadimah) provided by the husband. It first describes the clothing for a poor husband: in winter, a cotton shirt and a waist-wrapper; for a wealthy husband, similar but with a cloak. In summer, a shirt and waist-wrapper. Importantly, the servant is not given a khimar (headcover) because her head is not considered 'awrah (must-cover) in the Hanafi school, unlike the wife's head. She is given an izar (waist-wrapper) because she needs to go out. The mashayikh (scholars) note that what Imam Muhammad prescribed in the books is based on the customs of his time and place; clothing differs with climate and customs, so the judge should determine sufficiency accordingly. The passage also clarifies the definition of yasar (wealth) for this ruling: it is the nisab that prevents one from receiving charity (i.e., one who owns surplus wealth), not the nisab of zakat. If the husband and wife dispute over whether he is wealthy or poor, the husband's word is taken, unless the wife brings proof. If both bring proof, the wife's evidence is preferred. Finally, the author makes a crucial distinction: the servant's maintenance is owed in exchange for her service. If she refuses to do the work (cooking, etc.), she forfeits her maintenance. This is different from the wife's maintenance, which is owed in exchange for her confinement (ihtibas) to the marital home, regardless of whether she performs domestic work. This is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) from al-Dhakhirah.

Key Terms
الخمار (al-khimar): Headcover worn by women; the servant is not required to wear one because her head is not 'awrah.
الإزار (al-izar): Waist-wrapper or lower garment; prescribed for the servant because she goes out.
نصاب حرمان الصدقة (nisab hurman al-sadaqah): The threshold of wealth that prevents one from receiving charity; used to define yasar for providing a servant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key difference between the maintenance of a wife and that of a servant in Hanafi fiqh?
A) The wife's maintenance is fixed in dirhams, while the servant's is not.
B) The wife's maintenance is in exchange for confinement, while the servant's is in exchange for her work.
C) The servant's maintenance includes a khimar, but the wife's does not.
D) The servant's maintenance is higher than the wife's.

Key Takeaway
A servant's maintenance in Hanafi fiqh is conditional upon her service, and her clothing requirements are less than a wife's because her head is not 'awrah.

Clothing Obligations for Wife and Servant in Hanafi Fiqh
Specifies required clothing items for wife and servant based on season and wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required clothing items for a wife and a female servant according to the Hanafi school, and explain why the khimar is not obligatory for the servant.

Core Idea
The wife's head is 'awrah requiring khimar; the servant's head is not, so only an izar is obligatory for her.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the husband's obligations to provide clothing for his wife and female servant. It distinguishes between the two based on the concept of 'awrah and the nature of maintenance (for service vs. confinement). This lesson will walk you through the rulings and their rationale, emphasizing the role of custom and the judge's discretion.

Guided Path
1
Identify clothing items for the wife
List the specific garments prescribed for the wife in winter (shirt, warm garment, thick waist-wrapper, cheap cloak) and in summer (shirt and waist-wrapper). Note that a head covering (khimar) is also required.
The items for the wealthy (musir) are mentioned explicitly; for the impoverished (mu'sir) the text notes it is according to Muhammad's view.
2
Identify clothing items for the servant
Note that the servant is prescribed a waist-wrapper (izar) but not a khimar. The izar is needed because the servant goes out.
The absence of khimar is the key difference.
3
Understand the rationale for the difference
The text explains: the wife's head is 'awrah, so covering it is obligatory; the servant's head is not 'awrah, so covering it is not required.
This ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh and relates to the status of female slaves/servants.
4
Recognize the role of custom and the judge
The commentators note that the specific items mentioned by Muhammad are based on the customs of his time and place. The judge must consider sufficiency based on the time, place, and customs of the people.
This principle allows flexibility in different climates and cultures.
5
Distinguish the basis of maintenance for wife vs. servant
The wife's maintenance is in exchange for her confinement (ihtibas) to the marriage, so she receives it even if she does not work. The servant's maintenance is in exchange for her service (khidma); if she refuses to work, she forfeits her right.
This distinction is important for practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

In summer, a shirt like that and a waist-wrapper. And for the wealthy man in winter, a shirt and a [warm] garment and a thick waist-wrapper and a cheap cloak, and in summer a shirt like that and a waist-wrapper. Then he did not prescribe the head covering for the servant girl but prescribed it for the woman because the head covering is for covering the head, and the woman's head is 'awrah, and the servant's head is not 'awrah. And he prescribed for her the waist-wrapper because the servant needs to go out. Our scholars said: What Muhammad mentioned in the book regarding the servant's clothing is based on their customs, and that differs according to different places in severity of heat and cold and according to customs in each time. So the judge must consider sufficiency in the servant's maintenance regarding what is prescribed in every time and place. And what he mentioned about the clothing of the servant for the impoverished is only according to Muhammad's statement, as is not hidden. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: Wealth is measured by the nisab that prevents charity, not by the nisab of zakat. And if they differ about being wealthy or impoverished, the word is his (the husband's) unless the woman establishes evidence, and number and integrity are stipulated in this testimony, and the word 'shahada' is not stipulated. If both bring evidence, her evidence is preferred; as in al-Khaniyya. Then know that the maintenance of the servant is obliged upon the husband in exchange for service. If she refrains from cooking, baking, and household work, she does not deserve maintenance because what she deserves maintenance in exchange for does not exist, unlike the wife's maintenance, which is in exchange for confinement (ihtibas). So if she does not work, she deserves maintenance. This is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya); as in al-Dhakhira.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the clothing obligations for the wife and servant. For the wife, the husband must provide a shirt (qamis), waist-wrapper (izar), and head covering (khimar). For the servant, no head covering is required because her head is not 'awrah, but she needs an izar for outdoor activities. The specific items vary by season: winter requires warmer garments. The judge must consider local customs and sufficiency. The passage also discusses that the servant's maintenance is contingent on actual service, unlike the wife's maintenance which is for confinement (ihtibas). If the servant refuses work, she forfeits her right to maintenance.

Key Terms
الخمار (al-khimar): A head covering that conceals the hair and neck; prescribed for the wife but not for the servant.
الإزار (al-izar): A waist-wrapper or lower garment covering from waist to ankles; prescribed for both wife and servant.
العورة (al-'awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered; here specifically the head is 'awrah for the wife but not for the servant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the wife is free.
B) Because the wife's head is 'awrah while the servant's head is not.
C) Because the servant does not go out.
D) Because the wife is wealthier.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between wife and female servant in clothing obligations based on 'awrah and the basis of maintenance: wife's head is 'awrah requiring khimar, servant's head is not; wife's maintenance is for confinement, servant's is for service.

Nafaqah — Maintenance

Husband's Inability to Pay Maintenance: No Separation, Wife Ordered to Borrow
Explains Hanafi refusal to annul marriage for inability to pay maintenance and the wife's duty to borrow.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a husband's inability to pay maintenance, explain the reasoning, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, inability to pay maintenance does not dissolve the marriage; the wife must borrow on his credit.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key inter-madhhab dispute: what happens when a husband cannot provide maintenance? While the Shafi'i school allows judicial separation (tafriq), the Hanafi school insists the marriage remains intact and the wife borrows on his credit. We explore the reasoning behind this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Read the opening statement: the husband's inability to pay maintenance does not trigger separation; instead, the wife is ordered to borrow on his credit.
The ruling is preceded by the negation 'لا يفرق' (one does not separate).
2
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The author provides a comparative harm analysis: separation would nullify the husband's right, while delaying the wife's right is less harmful since maintenance becomes a debt by the judge's order.
The analogy to impotence is rejected because maintenance is subsidiary to procreation, the primary purpose of marriage.
3
Identify the opposing school and its dalil
The Shafi'i school allows tafriq on grounds of harm (darar) to the wife. The passage mentions this implicitly through the discussion of a Shafi'i judge's ruling.
The Shafi'i position is based on the principle that harm should be removed.
4
Examine the Hanafi response and intra-madhhab debates
The Hanafi response emphasizes that borrowing prevents harm and preserves the husband's rights. For absent husbands, some Hanafi scholars (e.g., Fath al-Qadir) allow annulment based on difficulty (ta'assur), but the mufta bihi rejects this.
The debate about the absentee husband shows the Hanafi school's rigor in requiring verified inability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, the wife stays married and borrows; in the Shafi'i school, she can obtain a judicial divorce.
The consequence affects the wife's marital status and the lender's right of recourse against the husband.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يفرق بعجزه عن النفقة وتؤمر بالاستدانة عليه لأنه لو فرق بينهما لبطل حقه ولو لم يفرق لتأخر حقها والأول أقوى في الضرر لأن النفقة تصير ديناً بفرض القاضي فيستوفي في الثاني وفوت المال وهو تابع في النكاح فلا يلحق بما هو المقصود وهو التوالد فلا يقاس العجز عن الإنفاق على العجز عن الجماع في المجبوب والعنيين. وأطلق في النفقة فشمل الأنواع الثلاثة فلا يفرق بعجزه عن كلها أو بعضها، وقيد بالنفقة ليعلم حكم المهر بالأولى. وفي غاية البيان معزياً إلى الفصول : إذا ثبت العجز بشهادة الشهود فإن كان القاضي شافعي المذهب وفرق بينهما نقذ قضاؤه بالتفريق، وإن كان حنيفاً لا ينبغي له أن يقضي بالتفريق بخلاف مذهبه إلا إذا كان مجتهداً ووقع اجتهاده على ذلك، فإن قضى مخالفاً لرأيه من غير اجتهاد فعن أبي حنيفة روايتان ولو لم يقض ولكن أمر شافعي المذهب ليقضي بينهما في هذه الحادثة فقضى بالتفريق نفذ إذا لم يرتش الآمر والمأمور فإن كان الزوج غائباً فرفعت المرأة الأمر إلى القاضي وأقامت المرأة البينة أن زوجها الغائب عاجز عن النفقة وطلبت من القاضي أن يفرق بينهما، فإن كان القاضي حنفياً فقد ذكرنا، وإن كان شافعياً ففرق بينهما قال مشاخ سمرقند جاز تفريقه لأنه قضى في فصلين مختلف فيهما التفريق بسبب العجز عن قوله : (فبقي على الأصل من اعتبار حاله قال في النهر : فيه نظر إذ لو اعتبر حاله فيه لوجب عليه نفقة لها إذا كان موسراً وهي فقيرة وقد علمنا أنها لا تجب قوله: (فشمل الأنواع الثلاثة) أي المأكول والكسوة والسكني. يصح النفقة والقضاء على الغائب، وكل واحد منهما مجتهد فيه . وقال ظهير الدين المرغيناني : لا هذا التفريق لأن القضاء على الغائب إنما يصح عند الشافعي وينفذ في إحدى الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة إذا ثبت المشهود به، وهنا لم يثبت المشهود به عند القاضي وهو العجز لأن المال غاد ورائج، ومن الجائز الغائب صار غنياً ولم يعلم به الشاهد لما بينهما من المسافة فكان الشاهد مجازفاً في هذه الشهادة. وقال صاحب الذخيرة : الصحيح لأنه لا قضاؤه لأن يصح العجز لا يعرف حالة الغيبة لجواز أن يكون قادراً فيكون هذا ترك الإنفاق لا للعجز عن الإنفاق، فإن رفع هذا القضاء إلى قاض آخر وأجاز قضاءه فالصحيح أنه لا ينفذ لأن هذا القضاء ليس بمجتهد فيه لما ذكرنا أن العجز لم يثبت ا.هـ. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بقوله: واعلم الفسخ إذا غاب ولم يترك لها نفقة يمكن بغير طريق إثبات عجزه بمعنى فقره وهو أن تتعذر النفقة عليها . قال القاضي أبو الطيب من الشافعية : إذا تعذرت النفقة عليها بغيبته ثبت لها الفسخ قال في الحلية وله وجه وجيه فلا يلزم مجيء ما قال ظهير الدين ا هـ . وهذا لا یرد ما قاله ظهير الدين لوجهين : الأول أنه ليس مذهب الشافعي. والثاني أن كلامه في التفريق بسبب العجز لا في غيره وفي الذخيرة فرق بين النفقة وبين سائر الديون في الأمر بالاستدانة فإن في سائر الديون من عليه الدين إذا عجز عن قضاء الدين لا يؤمر صاحب الدين بالاستدانة عليه وهنا بعد ما فرض القاضي لها تؤمر بالاستدانة على الزوج . والفرق بينهما أن المرأة لو لم تؤمر بالاستدانة عسى تموت جوعاً أو يموت الزوج فتسقط نفقتها فكان الأمر بها لتأكيد حقها وهذا المعنى معدوم في سائر الديون. قال مشايخنا : ليس فائدة الأمر بالاستدانة بعد فرض القاضي النفقة إثبات حق للمرأة عليه لأن حق رجوعها ثابت بالفرض، سواء أكلت من مال نفسها أو استدانت بأمر القاضي أو بغير أمره، ولكن فائدته أن يرجع الغريم على الزوج وبدون الأمر ليس له الرجوع عليه وإنما يرجع رب الدين على المرأة وهي ترجع بالمفروض على الزوج. وفي تجريد القدوري: أن فائدته أن تحيل المرأة الغريم على الزوج وإن لم يرض الزوج وبدونه لس لها ذلك . قوله : (بمعنى فقره الذي في الفتح «فقده» بالدال لا بالراء وهو الظاهر قوله : (الأول أنه ليس مذهب الشافعي) قال السيد أبو السعود في حاشية مسكين : نقل شيخنا عن الرملي في شرح المنهاج أن والده أفتى بعدم الفسخ فيما إذا تعذر تحصيل النفقة لغيبته وإن طالت وانقطع خبره قال : فقد صرح في الأم بأنه لا فسخ ما دام موسراً وإن انقطع خبره وتعذر استيفاؤها من ماله الخ. فقوله «موسراً» ظاهر في الفسخ عند عجزه وحينئذ يتجه ما ذكره شراح الهداية في الرد على الشافعي ثم قال : فالحاصل أنه استفيد من شرح غاية القصوى أن الاختلاف في الفسخ أي عند الشافعية وأن الأظهر عدمه بالنسبة لما إذا لم ينفق عليها حال غيبته والحال أن له قدرة على أداء النفقة، فإن عجز فلا
His saying: (And one does not separate due to his inability to pay maintenance, and she is ordered to borrow upon him) because if he separated between them, his right would be invalidated, and if he did not separate, her right would be delayed, and the first is stronger in harm because maintenance becomes a debt by the judge's imposition, so he recovers in the second, and loss of wealth is subsidiary in marriage, so it does not attach to what is the purpose, which is procreation, so inability to spend cannot be analogized to inability to have intercourse in the case of the impotent and the one with defective genitals. And he generalized in maintenance so it includes the three types, so one does not separate due to his inability to provide all or some of them, and he restricted it to maintenance so that the ruling of dower is known by priority. And in Ghayat al-Bayan citing al-Fusul: If inability is established by the testimony of witnesses, then if the judge is Shafi'i in madhhab and separates between them, his ruling of separation is enforced; and if he is Hanafi, it is not proper for him to rule with separation contrary to his madhhab unless he is a mujtahid and his ijtihad falls on that. If he rules contrary to his opinion without ijtihad, then from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations. And if he does not rule but orders a Shafi'i judge to rule between them in this incident and he rules with separation, it is enforced if the one who commands and the one commanded are not bribed. Then if the husband is absent and the woman raises the matter to the judge and establishes evidence that her absent husband is unable to pay maintenance, and she requests the judge to separate between them, then if the judge is Hanafi, we have mentioned; if he is Shafi'i and separates between them, the scholars of Samarkand said his separation is permissible because he judged in two matters in which there is disagreement: maintenance and judgment against an absentee, and each of them is a matter of ijtihad. Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani said: No, this separation is not valid because judgment against an absentee is only valid according to al-Shafi'i and is enforced in one of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa if the thing testified to is established. Here, the thing testified to (inability) is not established before the judge because wealth comes and goes, and it is possible that the absentee has become wealthy unknown to the witness due to distance, so the witness is being speculative in this testimony. The author of al-Dhakhira said: The correct view is that his judgment is not valid because inability cannot be known in the state of absence due to the possibility that he is able, so this would be abandonment of spending, not inability to spend. If this judgment is raised to another judge and he validates it, the correct view is that it is not enforced because this judgment is not a matter of ijtihad, as we mentioned that inability was not established. This was criticized in Fath al-Qadir by his saying: Know that annulment if he is absent and did not leave maintenance for her can be done without the method of establishing his inability meaning his poverty, which is that maintenance becomes difficult for her. Al-Qadi Abu al-Tayyib from the Shafi'is said: If maintenance becomes difficult for her due to his absence, annulment is established for her. Al-Hilya said: This has a strong aspect, so what Zahir al-Din said does not necessarily follow. This does not refute what Zahir al-Din said for two reasons: first, it is not the madhhab of al-Shafi'i; second, his words are about separation due to inability, not other reasons. In al-Dhakhira, a distinction is made between maintenance and other debts regarding the order to borrow: for other debts, the debtor's creditor is not ordered to borrow on the debtor's account, but here after the judge imposes maintenance, she is ordered to borrow on the husband. The difference is that if the woman were not ordered to borrow, she might die of hunger or the husband might die and her maintenance would be nullified, so the order is to emphasize her right; this meaning is absent in other debts. Our scholars said: The benefit of the order to borrow after the judge's imposition of maintenance is not to establish a right for the woman against him because her right of recourse is established by the imposition, whether she eats from her own wealth or borrows by the judge's order or without his order. Rather, its benefit is that the lender can have recourse against the husband, and without the order he does not have recourse against him; rather, the lender only has recourse against the woman, and she has recourse against the husband for the imposed amount. In Tajrid al-Quduri: Its benefit is that the woman can transfer the lender's claim to the husband even if the husband does not consent; without it she does not have that. His saying: (meaning his poverty in Fath al-Qadir: 'his lack' with dal not ra' and it is apparent). His saying: (First: it is not the madhhab of al-Shafi'i) al-Sayyid Abu al-Su'ud in Hashiyat Miskin said: Our teacher transmitted from al-Ramli in Sharh al-Minhaj that his father gave a fatwa of no annulment when obtaining maintenance is difficult due to his absence even if it is prolonged and his news is cut off. He said: For in al-Umm he explicitly stated that there is no annulment as long as he is wealthy even if his news is cut off and obtaining it from his wealth is difficult. So his saying 'wealthy' indicates annulment when he is unable, and then it aligns with what the commentators of al-Hidayah mentioned in refutation of al-Shafi'i. Then he said: The result is that it is understood from Sharh Ghayat al-Quswa that the disagreement regarding annulment is among the Shafi'is, and the apparent view is its non-occurrence when he does not spend on her during his absence while he has ability to pay maintenance; if he is unable, then...
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the matn statement that a husband's inability to pay maintenance does not warrant judicial separation (tafriq). Instead, the wife is ordered to borrow money on the husband's credit. The reasoning is that separation would annul the husband's right (his authority over the wife) and delay her right to maintenance; since maintenance becomes a debt when imposed by the judge, the latter option is less harmful. Unlike impotence, which directly affects procreation (the primary purpose of marriage), maintenance is ancillary. The ruling applies to all three types of maintenance: food, clothing, and housing. The passage then addresses a complex scenario: if a Shafi'i judge rules for separation based on proven inability, the ruling is enforced, but a Hanafi judge should not rule against his madhhab unless he is a mujtahid. Further, when the husband is absent, the Hanafi scholars differ: some argue that a Shafi'i judge's separation is invalid because inability cannot be verified for an absentee; others say that in such cases, the wife can seek annulment based on difficulty (ta'assur) rather than proven poverty. The passage ends by distinguishing the order to borrow in maintenance from other debts: the benefit allows the lender to directly claim from the husband, which is not possible otherwise.

Key Terms
التفريق (al-tafriq): Judicial separation (annulment of marriage) due to a defect or inability; here specifically for inability to pay maintenance.
الاستدانة (al-istidana): The wife's borrowing money on the husband's credit when he fails to provide maintenance, ordered by the judge.
العجز (al-'ajz): Inability to provide maintenance due to poverty or destitution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a husband is unable to pay maintenance, what is the wife instructed to do?
A) Seek immediate divorce.
B) Borrow money on the husband's credit.
C) Leave the house.
D) Wait patiently without any action.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a husband's inability to pay maintenance does not dissolve the marriage; the wife is ordered to borrow on his credit, allowing lender recourse against the husband.

The Benefit and Conditions of Ordering the Wife to Borrow for Maintenance
Explanation of the benefit and conditions of ordering a wife to borrow for maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge orders a wife to borrow for maintenance and identify the legal benefit of that order.

Core Idea
The judge's order to borrow turns the wife's debt into a claim against the husband.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a practical ruling in Hanafi fiqh: when a husband fails to pay maintenance and his wife has no means, the judge can order her to borrow. The key benefit is that the creditor can then directly claim from the husband. Understanding this ruling is essential for correct application of maintenance obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
The passage discusses the ruling on ordering the wife to borrow for maintenance after the judge has fixed the amount. Note that this only applies when the judge can actually fix maintenance.
The judge cannot fix maintenance for an absent insolvent husband with no present wealth.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
The condition 'after the judge has fixed maintenance' applies only when the judge can fix it; it does not apply to an absent insolvent husband with no present wealth, as the author will mention elsewhere.
This is a key limitation.
3
Correct the textual error
The matn says 'before he ordered him' but the correct expression is 'before he ordered her' referring to the wife.
Textual correction ensures accurate understanding.
4
Apply the ruling to the absent husband
Al-Ramli extends the same ruling to when the husband is absent and has no wealth with his relatives, so maintenance is impossible for her.
Expands the application.
5
Understand the alternative: ordering a wealthy relative
If a wealthy son or brother refuses to lend, the judge can fix maintenance directly on that relative and compel payment, as per al-Dhakhira.
This is an alternative remedy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بعد فرض القاضي النفقة) هذا القيد يظهر في غير مسألة المعسر الغائب لأن الغائب لا يفرض القاضي عليه نفقة ما لم يكن له مال حاضر كما سيذكره المصنف قوله : (قبل أن يأمره) كذا في النسخ وصواب التعبير يأمرها) بضمير المؤنث قوله : (لكن ذكر في شرح المختار الخ) قال الرملي : وكذا إذا كان الزوج غائباً ولا مال له عند من يقرّبه وتعذرت النفقة عليها كما هو ظاهر تأمل.
قوله : ( ويحبس الابن أو الأخ إذا امتنع سيأتي عند قول المتن «ولأبويه وأجداده» . عن الذخيرة : وإن أبى الابن أن يقرضها النفقة فرض لها عليه النفقة وتؤخذ منه وتدفع إليها لأن الزوج المعسر
His statement: (after the judge has fixed maintenance) this condition appears in a case other than that of the absent insolvent, because the judge does not fix maintenance for the absent unless he has present wealth, as the author will mention. His statement: (before he ordered him) is in the manuscripts; the correct expression is 'before he ordered her' with feminine pronoun. His statement: (but it is mentioned in Sharh al-Mukhtar etc.) Al-Ramli said: Similarly if the husband is absent and has no wealth with his relatives and maintenance is impossible for her, as is apparent upon reflection. His statement: (And the son or brother is imprisoned if he refuses) will come at the statement of the matn 'and for his parents and his grandparents'. From al-Dhakhira: If the son refuses to lend her the maintenance, then maintenance is fixed on him, and it is taken from him and given to her, because the insolvent husband...
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, focusing on the details of ordering the wife to borrow for maintenance. The author first clarifies a condition in the matn: 'after the judge has fixed maintenance' applies only when the judge has actually fixed it, which does not occur for an absent husband who has no present wealth (i.e., the judge cannot fix maintenance for a truly absent and insolvent man). Then he corrects a textual error: 'before he ordered him' should be 'before he ordered her'. Next, he cites al-Ramli's statement that the same ruling applies if the husband is absent and has no wealth with his relatives, so maintenance is impossible. Finally, he mentions a separate but related rule from al-Dhakhira: if a wealthy son (or brother) refuses to lend his mother (or sister) maintenance, the judge can fix maintenance on him directly, and it is taken from him and given to her. This is because the husband is insolvent (or absent), and the son's obligation is akin to that of a guardian. The passage ends abruptly, but the gist is clear: the wife can be ordered to borrow, and if a wealthy relative refuses to lend, they may be compelled to provide directly.

Key Terms
استدانة (istidana): The act of borrowing money or purchasing on credit for maintenance, authorized by the judge.
فائدة الأمر بالاستدانة (fa'idat al-amr bi al-istidana): The legal benefit of the judge's order to borrow: enabling the creditor to seek recourse from the husband.
ابن موسر (ibn musir): A wealthy adult son who is obligated to provide maintenance to his needy mother if her husband is unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The judge's order to borrow is essential to give the creditor recourse against the husband.

Nafaqah — Maintenance
intermediate

The Wife's Borrowing for Maintenance: Conditions and Liability
Explaining the ruling and benefits of the wife borrowing for maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on istidana and identify the conditions under which the husband becomes liable for the wife's debt.

Core Idea
The wife may borrow for maintenance, but the husband is only liable if she explicitly states or intends to borrow on his account.

When a husband fails to provide maintenance, the judge may permit the wife to borrow (istidana) to cover her needs. However, the husband's liability is not automatic. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on istidana, clarifying the benefits of this mechanism, the differences in definition, and the critical condition of explicit intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal mechanism
Recognize that istidana is the wife's act of borrowing or buying on credit for maintenance, with the expectation of reimbursement from the husband's property.
The judge's command to borrow gives the creditor recourse against the husband after death of either party.
2
Distinguish the two definitions
Note that al-Khassaf defines istidana as buying on credit (nasī'a), while Rukn al-A'imma al-Sabbughi defines it as borrowing (istiqrāḍ). Both are acceptable in practice.
The difference does not affect the ruling; the key is the wife's intention.
3
Determine the necessary condition for liability
The husband becomes liable only if the wife explicitly says 'I am borrowing on my husband's account' or intends to do so. Without explicit statement or intention, the debt is on the wife alone.
In case of dispute (she claims intention, he denies), the husband's word is taken.
4
Understand the wisdom behind commanding the wife
The judge commands the wife rather than the husband to borrow to avoid delay (harm) and because creditors are more willing to give credit to the wife (dual recourse against husband and wife).
This is a practical consideration to protect the wife's interests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع وذكر الحاكم في المختصر أن فائدته الرجوع على الزوج بعد موت أحدهما وبدونه لا رجوع . اهـ ما في الذخيرة فقد ذكر واللأمر بالاستدانة ثلاثة فوائد لكن من جعل فائدتها إمكان الإحالة عليه بدون رضاه ظاهره أنه ليس لرب الدين الأخذ من الزوج بدون الحوالة، وعلى الأول له ذلك كما لا يخفى ولم أر من ذكر الوجه في أمرها بالاستدانة دون أمره بذلك أنه المديون فكان ينبغي أن يأمره القاضي بالاستدانة، وقد ظهر لي وجهه بأنه لو أمر ربما تراخى في ذلك فيحصل لها الضرر فأمرت هي بالاستدانة لدفع الضرر، ولأن الغريم يطمئن لاستدانتها أكثر من استدانته باعتبار أنه يصير له المطالبة على شخصين الزوج والمرأة بخلاف استدانة الزوج فإنه لا يطالب إلا الزوج، فلو أمره القاضي بالاستدانة لنفقتها قبل أن يأمره لم يكن بعيداً، ولم أره منقولاً. واختلف في معنى الاستدانة فذكر الخصاف وتبعه الشارحون أنها الشراء بالنسيئة لتقضي الثمن من مال الزوج. وفي المجتبى معزياً إلى ركن الأئمة الصباغي أنها الاستقراض فإذا استدانت هل تصرح بأني أستدين على زوجي أو تنوي؟ أما إذا فظاهر وكذا إذا ،نوت، وإذا لم تصرح ولم تنو لا يكون الاستدانة عليه، ولو ادعت أنها نوت الاستدانة عليه وأنكر الزوج فالقول له .اهـ.
And the sage mentioned in al-Mukhtasar that its benefit is recourse against the husband after the death of one of them; without that, no recourse. End of what is in al-Dhakhira. So it has been mentioned that the command to borrow has three benefits. But whoever makes its benefit the possibility of referral to him without his consent, his apparent meaning is that the creditor does not have the right to take from the husband without assignment. According to the first, he has that right, as is not hidden. And I have not seen anyone mentioning the reason why she was commanded to borrow rather than him; that being that he is the debtor, so the judge should have commanded him to borrow. And its reason appeared to me: because if he commanded him, perhaps he would delay, causing harm to her, so she was commanded to borrow to ward off harm. And because the creditor is more comfortable with her borrowing than his borrowing, considering that he can then claim from two persons: the husband and the wife, unlike the husband's borrowing, where he can only claim from the husband. So if the judge had commanded him to borrow for her maintenance before commanding her, it would not have been far-fetched, but I have not seen it transmitted. And they differed on the meaning of borrowing: al-Khassaf and the commentators following him said it is buying on credit to be paid from the husband's property. And in al-Mujtaba, attributed to Rukn al-A'imma al-Sabbughi, that it is borrowing. So if she borrows, does she explicitly say 'I am borrowing on my husband' or does she just intend? As for if she is explicit, it is clear; similarly if she intends. If she does not explicitly say nor intend, it is not borrowing against him. If she claims she intended to borrow against him and the husband denies, the statement is his.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the wife borrowing for her maintenance when the husband is unable or absent. The author first discusses the benefit of the command to borrow: it gives the creditor recourse against the husband after death of either party. Then he lists three benefits of the command. He provides his own insight: the judge commands the wife to borrow rather than the husband to avoid delay and because creditors trust her more due to dual recourse. He then notes the difference of opinion on the definition of istidana: al-Khassaf says it is buying on credit, while al-Sabbughi says it is borrowing (qard). The passage clarifies that for the borrowing to be on the husband's account, the wife must explicitly state she is borrowing on his behalf or have that intention. If she claims intention but the husband denies, the husband's word is taken.

Key Terms
استدانة (istidāna): The wife's act of borrowing money or buying on credit for her maintenance, with the expectation of reimbursement from the husband's property.
النسيئة (al-nasī'a): Buying on credit, where payment is deferred.
الاستقراض (al-istiqrāḍ): Borrowing money with the promise of repayment.
الإحالة (al-iḥāla): Assignment of debt, where the creditor's claim is transferred to another party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Borrowing money (qard)
B) Buying on credit (nasī'a)
C) Selling property
D) Taking a loan with interest

Key Takeaway
The wife's borrowing for maintenance only obligates the husband if she explicitly states or intends to borrow on his account, and in case of dispute, her word is not taken without evidence.
